801 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. State


No. B14-86-00101-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


761 S.W.2d 384; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2388



September 22, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 180th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 438976.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of the offense of attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for attempted murder. The court found that appellant's motion to dismiss under the Speedy Trial Act was moot because the Act was held unconstitutional. The court found that in the absence of proof to the contrary, it was presumed that a jury followed the instructions given by the judge and appellant did not demonstrate that the jury failed to follow the instructions. The court found that appellant and her ex-husband were divorced at the time of trial. Thus, the ex-husband was fully competent to testify as to the events surrounding the alleged offense. The court found that the same evidence was elicited by appellant during cross-examination of the ex-husband as well as the complainant, and appellant was not in a position to complain on appeal. Thus, the court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for attempted murder was affirmed. Appellant did not demonstrate that the jury failed to follow the instructions given by the judge. Appellant and her ex-husband were divorced at the time of trial, thus the absolute prohibition against adverse spousal testimony was no longer applicable.

 

802 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moorman v. State


No. 01-87-00765-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2340



September 15, 1988 


NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 Harris County Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 956,820


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 Harris County, Texas, which found defendant guilty of selling obscene materials, pursuant to a plea of nolo contendere, and imposed sentence to four days confinement in the Harris County jail and a fine of $ 700.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded nolo contendere to a charge of selling obscene materials and was sentenced to four days confinement in the county jail and a fine of $ 700. Defendant appealed the judgment, arguing that the trial court erred in denying her pretrial motion to quash, arguing that the Texas Obscenity Statute violated U.S. Const. amend. I and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court held that defendant failed to state the portions of the statute that she believed to be unconstitutionally vague, either in itself or in the instant case, nor did defendant detail a risk or detriment to which she was exposed without fair warning. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that because defendant failed to enumerate a single example of unconstitutional application, the presumption of the statute's constitutionality remained unrebutted. The court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43.21(a)(1) (1988), which defined obscenity, was constitutional because it adopted the three-pronged approach and did not require a jury to determine a work's literary, artistic, political, and scientific value by the community's standards as perceived by an average person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for selling obscene materials because defendant failed to enumerate a single example of unconstitutional application of the Texas Obscenity Statute under the First and Fourteenth Amendments.

 

803 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Drummond v. State


Nos. 01-87-00766-CR, 01-87-00768-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2343



September 15, 1988 


NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 949,904 and 954,147


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of selling obscene materials after appellant pleaded nolo contendere.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere to and was convicted of selling obscene materials. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motion to quash because the Texas Obscenity Statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43(B)(1988) violated the U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding that appellant failed to mention what part of Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43 was vague, either in itself or as applied to appellant and failed to show a risk or detriment to which he had been exposed without fair warning. The court held that the statute was valid because it included the "average person applying community standards" language, specifically defined offenses, and the lack of serious literary, artistic, political, and scientific value factor. Additionally, appellant's motion to quash was properly denied because appellant failed to raise his constitutional argument in his motion to quash, which rendered the court jurisdictionally unable to address appellant's argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for selling obscene materials because appellant failed to assert which part of the Texas Obscenity Statute (statute) was vague either in itself or as applied to appellant, so the presumption of the statute's constitutionality remained unrebutted and appellant's motion to quash was properly denied.

Woodrome v. State


Nos. 01-87-00655-CR, 01-87-00656-CR, 01-87-00658-CR, 01-87-00659-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2350



September 15, 1988

Appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motion to quash because the Texas Obscenity Statute, Tex. Penal Code ch. 43(B) (1988) (statute) violated the U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. The court held that the statute was valid because it included the "average person applying community standards" language, specifically defined offenses, and the lack of serious literary, artistic, political, and scientific value factor. 805 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Renner v. State


No. 13-87-357-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


758 S.W.2d 890; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2395



September 15, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 347th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 347th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which found appellant guilty of aggravated sexual assault of a child and assessed punishment at life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of aggravated sexual assault of a child and was sentenced to life imprisonment. On review, appellant contended that the verdicts on guilt and punishment were invalid because they were rendered by less than 12 jurors, yet the verdict forms were not signed by them. Appellant also contended that the trial court erred in giving the jury a parole law charge pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1988). The court held that appellant waived any error in the form of the verdicts. However, the court set aside the trial court judgment based on the parole law charge and remanded to the trial court. The court held that it was unable to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole instruction made no contribution to the jury's assessment of the maximum allowable sentence, despite the aggravated nature of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court judgment convicting appellant of aggravated sexual assault and sentencing appellant to life imprisonment and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings. The court could not conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that the trial court's parole instruction did not contribute to the jury's assessment of the maximum allowable sentence.

 

806 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Owen v. State


No. A14-86-00640-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2275



September 8, 1988 


NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 434,627


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chief executive officer challenged the order of the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of the felony offense of theft of property, namely money.


OVERVIEW: Appellant chief executive officer, through agents and literature, represented to the complaining witnesses that their investments would make a profit. In 1983, the interest payments ceased, the company went bankrupt, and the investors lost their principle. Appellant was convicted and sentenced to ten years confinement for the felony offense of theft of property, namely money in excess of $ 10,000. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly admitted exhibits of appellant's financial records, because his objections to the chain of custody went to the weight of the evidence. The indictment, although it did not define "deprive," gave adequate notice of the offense. The court held that the intent to unlawfully deprive was established by sufficient evidence that appellant grossly misled investors into a false sense of security when the investments did not exist or were not used as represented. The court held that, given the curative instruction and devastating consequences for owners who lost their life savings, the punishment was reasonable and not the product of unfair bias resulting from the unconstitutional parole instruction laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for theft, because the indictment gave adequate notice of the offense, sufficient evidence established the intent of appellant chief executive officer to unlawfully deprive the owners of their money, and the instruction on the unconstitutional parole law was harmless error.

 

807 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. C14-87-00501-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2282



September 8, 1988 


NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 469,955


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, for possession of heroin.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped for a traffic violation. When the officer discovered that appellant had outstanding warrants, appellant was arrested and a search revealed heroin. Appellant was convicted of possession of heroin. Appellant sought review, contending that the jury instructions required that the heroin be admitted into evidence, a discrepancy in the chain of custody caused reasonable doubt, and the record failed to show that appellant knew the substance was heroin. Appellant also contended that there was no probable cause for the arrest, the jury was erroneously instructed under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, and the trial court erred by including in the judgment the date the offense was committed. The court affirmed and held that the jury instructions did not require that heroin be admitted into evidence, the chain of custody was sufficiently established, and the amount of heroin in appellant's possession was enough to prove knowledge. In addition, the court held that there was sufficient probable cause, the search was incident to a lawful custodial arrest, the jury instruction was harmless error, and the inclusion of the date of the offense was not error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for possession of heroin because the heroin did not need to be introduced into evidence, the evidence sufficiently established chain of custody, and the evidence showed that appellant knew that heroin was in his possession. In addition, the court held that the arrest and search of appellant were lawful, the jury instruction constituted harmless error, and it was proper to include the date of the offense.

 

808 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Winborne v. Commissioners' Court of Ellis County


No. 10-88-078-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


757 S.W.2d 876; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2258



September 1, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 40th Judicial District Court, Ellis County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the judgment of the 40th Judicial District Court of Ellis County, Texas, which refused to grant a writ of mandamus against appellee commissioners'court forcing appellee to order a rollback election pursuant to Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. § 26.07.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer petitioned appellee commissioners'court for a rollback election on property taxes appellee had imposed, was denied and sought a writ of mandamus in the trial court to force the election, which was denied. On appeal, the court reversed and held that Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. § 26.07 was constitutional and allowed appellant and the other voters of the county to call for a rollback election when appellees promulgated a tax rate higher than that contained in § 26.07. The court found that the right of appellant to petition was expressly excepted out of the general powers of government in Tex. Const. art. I, § 2,27 and that the rollback election was mandated by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the refusal of the trial court to grant a writ of mandamus against appellee commissioners'court because appellant taxpayer had the right to call for a rollback election under state law.

 

809 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rische v. State


No. 01-86-00671-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


757 S.W.2d 518; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2203



August 31, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion For Rehearing Overruled October 7, 1988 .


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court No. 419, 614.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) remanded the cause in which appellant was adjudicated guilty of voluntary manslaughter for reconsideration of the harm caused appellant by the inclusion of an unconstitutional parole instruction in the trial court's jury charge at the conclusion of the punishment phase.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of voluntary manslaughter. The trial court gave only the statutory parole instruction in the jury charge at the conclusion of the punishment phase. In light of new rulings that held the statutory parole instruction to be unconstitutional, the Court of Criminal Appeals remanded the cause. It directed the court to reconsider the harm caused appellant by the inclusion of the parole instruction despite of the fact that appellant made no specific and timely objection as to the unconstitutionality of the charge at trial. The court applied the standard of review in Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). The court reversed and held it could not determine beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury did not consider the unconstitutional parole charge in deciding to assess a punishment against appellant that was in excess of the minimum allowed by law. The court was required to reverse the case and remand it to the trial court for a new trial on punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the cause for new trial on punishment only because the trial court erred and included the unconstitutional parole instruction to the jury in the punishment stage of the trial, and the court could not say the instruction did not contribute to the punishment assessed against appellant.

 

810 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gordon v. State


No. 01-87-01014-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


757 S.W.2d 496; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2206



August 31, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Court Criminal Court At Law No. 1 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 05863040.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the Criminal Court At Law No. 1 of Harris County, Texas, for operating an adult arcade without a permit in violation of Houston, Tex., Ordinance 85-1337, and alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague, unconstitutionally overbroad, violated due process of law and constituted an impermissible prior restraint on free speech, and was void under the Texas Constitution and preemption doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of operating an adult arcade without a permit in violation of Houston, Tex., Ordinance 85-1337. Appellant alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad on its face and as applied, violated due process of law and constituted an impermissible prior restraint on free speech, and was void under the Texas Constitution and under the doctrine of preemption because of its inconsistency with state legislation which provided for the regulation, taxation, and zoning of coin-operated machines and regulated the location of sexually oriented commercial activities. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court held that the ordinance was not vague because it provided standards that were capable of objective measurement and gave fair notice of the conduct required and prohibited. The court found that the ordinance was not overbroad. The court ruled that the ordinance merely regulated the manner in which an adult arcade may operate and did not offend the U. S. Const. amend. I. Finally, the court determined that there was no conflict between the ordinance and the state legislation therefore the ordinance was not void or preempted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because the city ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad, it did not offend the First Amendment but merely regulated the manner in which an adult arcade may operate, and was not void or preempted because there was no conflict between the ordinance and state laws which provided for the regulation, taxation, and zoning of coin-operated machines.

 

811 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


McNiel v. State


No. 01-87-0641-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


757 S.W.2d 129; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2220



August 31, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 351st District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 455,621.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 351st Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of misdemeanor theft by receiving after she bought used car seats for resale but failed to obtain a warranty of good title.


OVERVIEW: Appellant worked at her husband's auto accessory store and bought used car seats for resale but failed to obtain a warranty of good title from the individual. The car seats later proved to be stolen and appellant was convicted of misdemeanor theft by receiving stolen property. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(c)(3) provided fair notice of the requirements and was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 2.05(2)(B), the jury was permitted to presume that appellant knew the car seats were stolen if she failed to do any of the three acts required of her under § 31.03(c)(3), and that, therefore, the presumption was not unconstitutionally irrational and arbitrary. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction because the properly qualified expert testified that the fair market value of the car seats was actually higher than the amount for which she was charged. Because the state filed no controverting affidavit, appellant was entitled to a per se change of venue but waived that right by not objecting and pursuing fact issues at the venue hearing.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction of theft by receiving was affirmed because the statute clearly required that she obtain a warranty of good title and the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or arbitrary.

 

812 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Salas v. State


No. 13-87-398-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


756 S.W.2d 832; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2229



August 31, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 94th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile offender challenged the order of the 94th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which denied his motion to suppress his confession which was obtained in violation of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.12, convicted him of murder, and which gave the jury an unconstitutional jury instruction during the punishment phase.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile offender was charged with murder and certified as an adult. At trial the jury rejected his self-defense claim and convicted him of murder. In the punishment phase the trial court instructed the jury in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4(a) which the Court of Criminal Appeals had struck down as unconstitutional. Appellant challenged his conviction. The court reversed the judgment because it could not determine beyond a reasonable doubt that the error in the jury instruction made no contribution to the punishment of appellant. Appellant's written confession was obtained in violation of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. art. 52.02 but the court held the error in admitting the confession into evidence was not reversible because the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that the error made no contribution to appellant's conviction and punishment. Evidence that the arresting officers violated Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.12 was first raised in appellants motion for new trial. It did not meet the test for newly discovered evidence and if there was any error in the trial court's failure to admit the evidence the court found it was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction of appellant juvenile offender because the trial court gave the jury an unconstitutional instruction during the punishment phase of the trial. The cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

813 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Guerra v. State


No. 13-86-526-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


760 S.W.2d 681; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2248



August 31, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Denial of Rehearing November 10, 1988, Reported at: 760 S.W.2d 681 at 698.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 24th District Court of Jackson County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 24th District Court of Jackson County (Texas), convicting appellant of engaging in organized criminal activity involving an extensive drug ring. The appeal raised 37 points of error.


OVERVIEW: The court overruled 36 of appellant's 37 points of error on appeal. Appellant's crime was a serious one, and the jury could easily have found that appellant repeatedly committed drug offenses throughout the course of organized criminal activity. There were sufficient facts in an affidavit for the warrant issuing magistrate to find probable cause that appellant was committing felony offenses and that an interception of his phone calls would provide evidence of such crimes. The state showed that appellant was organizing the transfer of hundreds of pounds of marihuana. From appellant's residence, appellant would arrange the transfer of marihuana he had purchased to persons in Florida, Houston, and Austin. Numerous individuals were involved in appellant's network. The court agreed with appellant's last point of error that he suffered egregious harm because in his final argument, the prosecutor referred to the parole charge and explained how parole eligibility was determined, which was unconstitutional. Because the court was not convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that the parole charge made no contribution to the punishment, it vacated the judgment and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court based on an error which occurred in the punishment phase of trial. Accordingly, the judgment of conviction was ordered set aside and appellant was remanded to the custody of the sheriff to answer the indictment in the case.

 

814 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Henson v. Jarmon


No. 12-88-00046-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


758 S.W.2d 368; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2252



August 31, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2 SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant heirs challenged a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2, Smith County (Texas), declaring appellees illegitimate daughters the sole heirs of intestate decedent's estate. Appellants claimed the trial court erred in retroactively applying a 1987 amendment to Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 42(b).


OVERVIEW: In a jury trial, appellees illegitimate daughters were found the sole heirs of intestate decedent. Appellant heirs sought review of the judgment, claiming that the trial court erred in retroactively applying an amendment to Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 42(b). The amendment allowed a child to prove his heirship by showing he was a biological child. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that no litigant had a vested right in a statute which affected remedy or was procedural in nature and affected no vested substantive right. Further, the court held that the interest in finality was not affected by application of the amendment prior to distribution of the estate, and the application of the statute as it existed on the date of death would have deprived appellees equal treatment under the law, under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: Judgment finding appellees illegitimate daughters the sole heirs of a deceased intestate was affirmed because appellant heirs had no vested rights prior to distribution of the estate, and retroactive application of an amended statute afforded appellees equal protection under the law.

 

815 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cole v. State


No. 06-87-058-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


757 S.W.2d 864; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2177



August 30, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 71st Judicial District Court of Harrison County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 71st Judicial District Court of Harrison County, Texas, which placed defendant on deferred adjudication for the offense of possession of cocaine and which later revoked defendant's probation and imposed sentencing, alleging the trial court erred in imposing a predetermined sentence in violation of defendant's right to due process.


OVERVIEW: Following a plea of not guilty to the charge of possession of cocaine, defendant was placed on deferred adjudication. The trial judge warned defendant that it would impose a 75-year sentence if defendant's probation was revoked. Defendant made no objections to the trial court's comment. Later, the state initiated an adjudication of guilt and proceedings to revoke defendant's probation when he violated his probation terms. Various witnesses testified on defendant's behalf during the revocation hearing. At sentencing, the trial court referenced its previous warning to defendant and imposed a 75-year sentence as the trial court had threatened to impose if defendant's probation was revoked. Defendant made no objections to the sentencing. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held the trial judge's comments when granting deferred adjudication and when assessing punishment indicated that he had impermissibly determined defendant's sentence prior to considering defendant's presentation of mitigating evidence; but because defendant failed to object to the punishment or to the procedures used by the trial court, any due process violation was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment revoking defendant's probation and imposing sentencing and held the trial court's comments during the granting of the deferred adjudication and during the sentencing indicated it impermissibly predetermined defendant's sentence prior to considering mitigation evidence; and defendant waived any violation of his due process rights by failing to object during the granting of the deferred adjudication or sentencing.

 

816 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Florio v. State


No. C14-86-00849-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


758 S.W.2d 351; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2135



August 25, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 10th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 85CR520.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 10th Judicial District Court of Galveston County, Texas, which convicted appellant of injury to a child by omission and sentenced him to 60 years in prison after he abused and killed his girlfriend's two-year-old son.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was left to care for his girlfriend's two-year-old son while she worked, and was later convicted of injury to a child by omission after the child died from abusive injuries. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and held that appellant could have been found guilty under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04 (Supp. 1988) without proof that he had a duty toward the child because omission was an element of that offense and Tex. Penal Code § 6.01(c) (1974) required a duty be found only where omission was not an element. The court found that § 22.04 was not impermissibly vague as applied to appellant because his U.S. Const. amend. I rights were not at issue and appellant's conduct was the type of hard-core conduct which would have been prohibited under any construction of the statute. The court also held that appellant was a person of ordinary intelligence who had fair notice that his failure to provide medical care to the victim under the circumstances subjected him to criminal liability under § 22.04. There was sufficient evidence to show that appellant took responsibility for the child by living as a family together and caring for the child while the mother was at work.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant defendant's conviction for injury to a child by omission because the state was not required to prove that appellant had a duty under the statute and there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict and to show that appellant had agreed to care for the child.

 

817 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


De Leon v. State


No. C14-86-930-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


758 S.W.2d 621; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2136



August 25, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 12th District Court of Walker County, Cause No. 13,468.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 12th Judicial District Court of Walker County, Texas, which convicted him of murder pursuant to a jury verdict and sentenced him to 99 years in prison, after appellant stabbed another inmate 51 times in order to carry out a prison gang contract hit.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stabbed another inmate 51 times pursuant to a prison gang contract hit and was found guilty of murder. Both appellant and his attorney filed briefs on appeal, but the court held that there was no right of hybrid representation in Texas and that it was not required to consider appellant's pro se brief. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that appellant's confession was properly admitted because the prison guard's question about the whereabouts of the murder weapon was not reasonably calculated to elicit appellant's response of "I killed him" as prohibited by Miranda. The court also held that if the guard's query was custodial interrogation which required Miranda warnings, it came under the public safety exception to the rule. The court found that appellant failed to properly support his motion for change of venue with two credible persons' affidavits and that his motions to quash the indictment were properly denied. Display of appellant's tattoo did not violate the right against self-incrimination and the trial court had discretion to determine whether leg irons were appropriate for restraining appellant's witnesses.


OUTCOME: Appellant 's conviction for murder was affirmed because his confession was properly admitted as the query of the prison guard to ascertain the whereabouts of the murder weapon could not have been reasonably calculated to elicit appellant's actual response.

 

818 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lawson v. State


No. 01-85-00186-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


757 S.W.2d 122; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2162



August 25, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 21st District Court, Burleson County; Harold Towslee, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court of criminal appeals reversed and vacated the court of appeals judgment that affirmed appellant's conviction of aggravated sexual assault in the 21st District Court, Burleson County (Texas) because appellant's right to confrontation was violated by the erroneous admission of a videotape of a child's testimony in a sexual assault case.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of aggravated assault. The court of criminal appeals reversed and vacated the court's judgment that affirmed appellant's conviction. The court of criminal appeals remanded to the court for a determination on whether the trial court's error in admitting the evidence of the videotape of the child's testimony contributed beyond a reasonable doubt to appellant's conviction. On remand, the court held the trial court did err in admitting the videotape because it violated appellant's right to confrontation when the child was never produced in court for cross-examination. Next, the court held that the error required reversal because the court was not able to say beyond a reasonable doubt that the videotape made no contribution to appellant's conviction. The court after viewing all of the evidence in the light most favorable to the jury's verdict found the evidence sufficient for establishing the elements of aggravated sexual assault. The court reversed appellant's conviction because the trial court erred in admitting the videotape, and the error contributed to appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction of aggravated sexual assault because the videotape of the child's testimony was erroneously admitted, and its admission contributed to appellant's conviction.

 

819 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Pike v. State


Nos. 10-86-065-CR, 10-86-066-CR, 10-86-137-CR, 10-86-138-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


758 S.W.2d 357; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2440



August 25, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 249th Judicial District Court, Johnson, County, Texas, Trial Court Nos. 24952, 24953, 24956, 24957.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the orders of the 249th Judicial District Court of Johnson County (Texas), which found them guilty of conspiracy to commit the aggravated manufacture of methamphetamine and the aggravated delivery of methamphetamine, and assessed punishment. Defendants claimed that the jury instructions and certain irrelevant testimony were inflammatory, prejudicial, and resulted in an unfair trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with organized criminal activity. A motion for severance was denied and defendants were found guilty after a jury trial. Defendants appealed. The court held that the girls' testimony that they paid for drugs by having sex with one defendant was relevant as proof that the conspiracy to deliver had been carried out, and was direct evidence of an act by one co-conspirator in furtherance of the conspiracy. The court found that the testimony was not prejudicial and inflammatory, was properly admitted as evidence of the guilt of both defendants, was not a basis to grant a motion for severance, and the joint trial did not result in prejudice to either. The court found that there was no error in refusing an instruction as to photographs withdrawn that were otherwise admissible. The court affirmed the judgments of conviction and held that considering the nature of the offenses, the facts proven, including the overwhelming evidence of guilt, the jury instructions did not contribute to the punishments assessed, were not harmful, and defendants were not denied a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction were affirmed because considering the nature of the offenses, the facts proven, including the overwhelming evidence of guilt, the jury instructions did not contribute to the punishments assessed, were not harmful, and defendants were not denied a fair and impartial trial.

 

820 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Buckley v. State


No. 6-87-088-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


758 S.W.2d 339; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1562



 August 23, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Withdrawn and Substituted August 23, 1988. Motion for Rehearing Overruled. Dissenting Opinion on Motion For Rehearing August 23, 1988. Reported at: 758 S.W.2d 339 at 349.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 276th Judicial District Court of Morris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 276th Judicial District Court of Morris County (Texas), for aggravated sexual assault alleging that the trial court erred in admitting evidence pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.072, because the statute violated his constitutional right to confront his accuser as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI and U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. 1, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the aggravated sexual assault of his minor daughter, which he appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in admitting his older daughter's testimony as to the minor daughter's account of the assault, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.702 (1988). Defendant asserted his constitutional right to confrontation. On appeal, the court held that the testimony qualified under a form of child-victim hearsay exception set out in art. 38.702 and under the circumstances was constitutional because the minor daughter spontaneously told her older sister of the assault, the child was not presented in court through visual electronic medium, and the state called the child in the case-in-chief to verify her statements and to allow cross-examination. The court found that the lower court satisfied the requirement of testing the statement's reliability and that the facts of the case supported the lower court's findings.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault was affirmed on the grounds that a statutory child-victim hearsay exception was constitutionally applied and allowed state to admit into evidence defendant's older daughter's testimony as to his minor daughter's account of the assault.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 178th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery, and entered a restitution order as a condition of appellant's parole.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of aggravated robbery. Appellant argued that insufficient evidence supported his conviction because the only witness who identified appellant was an accomplice witness whose testimony was not sufficiently corroborated. On appeal, the court found that after eliminating the accomplice witness' testimony, the remaining evidence sufficiently linked appellant to the robbery. Next, the court held that appellant's objection to a police officer's hearsay testimony was not preserved for review because appellant did not offer any reason for not objecting before the answer was given. The court held that the jury instruction concerning parole eligibility pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4 (1988) was not reversible error because it did not affect appellant's punishment. The court found appellant's claim of error to the trial court's restitution order was without merit. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because sufficient evidence supported appellant's conviction of aggravated robbery, and there was no reversible error in the jury instruction concerning parole eligibility, and in the restitution order.

Thomas v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston

August 18, 1988

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 228th District Court Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery by using or exhibiting a deadly weapon, contending reversal of judgment due to ineffective assistance of counsel and error in jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought reversal of his conviction for aggravated robbery by using or exhibiting a deadly weapon on the grounds that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. Appellant claimed that his counsel was not acquainted with the law concerning impeachment and cross-examination of defense witnesses and was not prepared to preserve the defense strategy from improper assault by the prosecutor. Appellant also claimed that the lower court erred by submitting to the jury, at the punishment phase, the parole instructions set out in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a), which violated the separation of powers doctrine and denied him due process of law. On appeal, the court held that appellant's counsel's performance was not deficient as counsel timely objected to prosecutor assaults during defense witness questioning and any harm caused was corrected by instructions to disregard. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 was ruled unconstitutional but the lower court's jury instructions to ignore matters concerning parole was a harmless error as it was a curative instruction to the jury did not affect appellant's sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed on the grounds that appellant failed to show deficient performance in counsel's representation and error in jury instructions was harmless as instruction was curative and given the facts of the case, did not affect appellant's sentence.

 

823 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Vinson v. Burgess


No. 2-87-069-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


755 S.W.2d 481; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2279



August 18, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 755 S.W.2d 481 at 484.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 211TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. Original Opinion of January 14, 1988, Reported at: 755 S.W.2d 481. Opinion on Rehearing Filed May 12, 1988, Reported at: 755 S.W.2d 483 at 484.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants filed a motion for rehearing with the Court of Appeals of Texas, Second District, Fort Worth (Texas), following its grant of appellee's motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed a motion for rehearing contending the court erred in holding that Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 21(a) did not authorize the tax rollback system of Tex. Prop. Tax Code § 26.07 and by finding that § 26.07 was unconstitutional because it was a constitutional legislative enactment of the Texas bill of rights. The court denied the motion for rehearing. It held that since the legislature could not delegate the powers conferred upon it by the constitution to the people to exercise by direct election, then it also had no power to delegate the powers conferred upon other governmental bodies, such as commissioners courts, to the people to exercise by direct election. The court noted that although all power was inherent to the people by virtue of Tex. Const. art. I, § 2, they did not resume their inherent power or any delegated power by virtue of Tex. Const. art. I, § 27; that § 27 instead provided for the right of the people to make their wishes known by assembly, petition, address, or remonstrance.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellants' motion for rehearing because the tax rollback system was unconstitutional since the legislature had no power to delegate the powers conferred upon other governmental bodies to the people to exercise by direct election.

 

824 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Olivarez v. State


Appeal No. 04-86-00405-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


756 S.W.2d 113; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2300



August 17, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 226th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 86-CR-0881 Honorable Ted Butler, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 226th District Court of Bexar County, Texas, which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a judgment of conviction in an aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon case. On appeal, the court reversed and held that Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 was a violation of the separation of powers doctrine of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1 and was unconstitutional. The court found that it was clear that it was likely that the jury did consider appellant's criminal history. The contribution of appellant's criminal record to the 45 year sentence did not establish beyond a reasonable doubt that the erroneously given instruction made no contribution to the punishment. Although it was proper to instruct the jury that the law placed the burden of proof on the state, it was not reversible error to omit this specific instruction from the charge when the charge, read as a whole, adequately informed the jury on the issue of burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon because the court found that it could not hold beyond a reasonable doubt that an erroneous instruction had no affect on appellant's punishment.

Hensley v. State

828 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Barton v. State


No. B14-87-00500-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2002



August 11, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Cause No. 450,141 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault of his 13-year old step-granddaughter. He contended that the trial court erred in allowing a district court judge to testify as a character witness, and by including, over defendant's objection, the parole charge required under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of his 13-year old step-granddaughter. Defendant appealed his conviction, claiming that the trial court erred in permitting a district court judge to testify as a character witness, and that the trial court erred by including, over defendant's objection, the parole charge required under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a). The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. While Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 605 prevented a judge from testifying at a trial over which he presided, a judge was not prohibited from serving as a witness in all cases solely because of his position. The probative value of the testifying judge's testimony was not outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice. The testifying judge's interaction with the parties was personal and in no way connected with his duties as a criminal judge. The court also found that the trial court's inclusion of the parole charge mandated by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) was error, but not reversible, because it also found, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the submission of the parole charge made no contribution to defendant's punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sexual assault conviction. It was not error for the trial court to permit a district court judge to testify where his interaction with the parties was of a personal nature and not connected to his position as a judge. Further, the trial court's error in giving a parole charge to the jury was not reversible because the submission of the parole charge did not contribute to defendant's punishment.

Childers v. State


No. B14-87-00071-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2004



August 11, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 21st District Court Washington County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 9,585


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor challenged his conviction from the 21st District Court, Washington County (Texas), for the felony of hindering a secured creditor. Appellant had granted the bank a security interest in seven vehicles, items of office furniture, and his company's accounts receivable and failed to deliver any of the collateral items to the bank after it sued and recovered a summary judgment authorizing it to levy execution on its collateral.


OVERVIEW: Appellant debtor based his objections to the sufficiency of the evidence to support the charge of hindering a secured creditor on both the transferring and the disposing theories. The court held that there was sufficient evidence from which the jury could have concluded, beyond a reasonable doubt, that appellant disposed of the collateral to which the bank was entitled by appropriating or exercising control over it. The court concluded that the statute sufficiently specified the requisite mental state and that failure to define terms would not categorically render a statute unconstitutionally vague. The court also held that the statute gave a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice of the conduct it proscribed and was not unconstitutionally vague or uncertain. The court found that the trial court properly included two definitions in its charge, consistent with the alternate theories of committing the offense as alleged: disposal or transfer. The court concluded that the evidence developed during trial sufficiently raised the defensive issue of whether appellant acted alone or as a representative of his business, to justify the law of parties charge. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Appellant debtor had fair notice of the conduct proscribed. There was sufficient evidence, beyond a reasonable doubt, that appellant disposed of the collateral by appropriating or exercising control over it.

Gil v. State


No. 3-87-006-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


756 S.W.2d 108; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2356



August 10, 1988  
August 10, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMAL COUNTY, 274TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR-85-210-C, HONORABLE CHARLES R. RAMSAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a conviction for aggravated assault entered by the District Court of Comal County, 274th Judicial District (Texas). The jury assessed punishment at six years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of aggravated assault and sentenced him to six years imprisonment. The trial court charged the jury in accordance with the parole law provisions of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1988) and instructed the jury not to consider the manner in which the parole law might be applied to defendant. At the evidentiary hearing on defendant's motion for a new trial, defendant introduced an affidavit of one of the jurors, which indicated that the jury disobeyed the instruction and fashioned defendant's sentence based on the parole law. The trial court overruled defendant's motion for a new trial. The court applied the harm test set forth in Tex R. App. P. Ann. 81(b)(2) (1988), which required an appellate court to reverse a judgment where the record showed error below, unless the court determined beyond a reasonable doubt that the error made no contribution to the punishment. In reversing the judgment and remanding the matter, the court held that the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion for a new trial where uncontroverted evidence established that the jury violated the court's instruction not to consider the parole law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of aggravated assault and sentencing him to six years imprisonment because the court found that defendant was harmed by the jury's failure to obey the trial court's instruction regarding the parole law. The court remanded the matter for a new punishment hearing.

Crawford v. State


No. 01-87-00542-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


755 S.W.2d 554; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1886



August 4, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 179th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 461,174.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 179th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which found appellant guilty of murder with a deadly weapon and assessed punishment at life imprisonment after appellant pled true to two enhancement paragraphs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of murder with a deadly weapon and pled true to two enhancement paragraphs, and the jury assessed punishment at life imprisonment. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in submitting the parole charge, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1988), during the punishment phase of the trial. The court affirmed, even though the statute was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers and due course of law provisions of the Texas constitution, because according to Tex. R. App. P. § 81(b)(2), appellant was not harmed by the inclusion of the charge. The court found that the facts of the case included, among other things, appellant's written confession as the heinous murder. The trial court had clearly stated that the operation of the parole law was not to be considered by the jurors, which was a curative instruction, and the jury found two enhancement paragraphs to be true.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of murder with a deadly weapon and assessing punishment at life imprisonment, because the giving of an unconstitutional parole instruction made no contribution to the punishment assessed, because the trial court gave a curative instruction that the jury was not to consider the issue of parole, the facts of the case were heinous, and the jury found two enhancement paragraphs to be true.

Demetriou v. State

NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 863,630; 863,631; 863,632.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7, Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of three misdemeanor offenses arising out of the same incident. Appellant was found guilty of resisting arrest, carrying a weapon, and criminal trespass in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 38.03, 46.02, 30.05, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of resisting arrest, carrying a weapon, and criminal trespass in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 38.03, 46.02, 30.05, respectively. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the state established that appellant carried a handgun "on or about" her person and that there was sufficient circumstantial evidence linking appellant to the gun, on which the jury could base its conclusion that appellant knowingly carried a weapon in her automobile. Sufficient evidence showed appellant resisted arrest and intentionally remained on the trespassed property after receiving notice to leave from deputies with "apparent authority," a term which did not have to be defined for the jury. There was no grounds for a mistrial related to the prosecutor's comments related to appellant's failure to testify. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.08. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by not allowing appellant to cross-examine the complaining witness, who had filed a civil suit against appellant, and excluding such evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction of resisting arrest, carrying a weapon, and criminal trespass, and held there was sufficient circumstantial evidence linking appellant to the gun on which the jury could base a conclusion that appellant knowingly carried a weapon in her automobile. The court found sufficient evidence to show that appellant resisted arrest and committed the trespass.

Turner v. State


No. 01-86-00195-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3446



August 4, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Court At Law No. Two of Brazoria County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 47,578


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the County Court At Law No. Two of Brazoria County (Texas), which convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-1(2)(A)(B) (Supp. 1988).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-1(2)(A)(B) (Supp. 1988). The lower court convicted appellant, sentencing him to two years probation, 30 days confinement, and payment of a fine. Appellant challenged his conviction, contending that the lower court erred in admitting the results of his blood-alcohol tests and evidence that an alcohol concentration of 0.10 was statutory proof of intoxication. Moreover, appellant failed to show that an objectionable venireman served on the jury.

834 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gabriel v. State


No. 01-87-00889-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


756 S.W.2d 68; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2437



August 4, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 475,864, DON SHIPLEY, Judge.

Opinion of June 23, 1988 Withdrawn and Substituted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of armed robbery. Appellant claimed the trial court erred by instructing the jury on a parole charge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1988), which was declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge provided a jury instruction which included an unconstitutional parole charge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1988) at appellant's trial for aggravated robbery. Appellant did not object. The court affirmed the conviction and held that appellant's failure to object waived the error. This prohibited appellant from obtaining a windfall because appellant may have guessed that appellant would have received a lesser sentence had the jury been aware of the time appellant would have served. However, had the appellant objected to the instruction, the court would have reversed the conviction absent proof that the jury was not prejudiced by the instruction and appellee would have had the burden to show that there was no prejudice so as to avoid inconsistent results and to provide an objective test to determine if a conviction should have been reversed. The court found that the state should have the burden to show that there was no prejudice because of the difficulty of determining whether the jury was improperly prejudiced by the instruction because Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 606(b) prohibited a juror from testifying as to statements made during deliberations..


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because appellant failed to object to the improper jury instruction, which included an unconstitutional parole charge, to avoid a potential windfall based upon appellant's strategy not to object so that appellant could have received a lesser sentence if the jury had known that appellant would have to serve a certain portion of the sentence.

Lopez v. State


No. 01-87-01017-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


756 S.W.2d 49; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1771



July 28, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for discretionary review ref'd. November 30, 1988. Motion for rehearing on petition for discretionary review denied, January 25, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Law No. 12 Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 1419


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Harris County Criminal Court at Law (Texas), which affirmed the trial court's decision convicting him of operating an adult arcade without a permit and assessed a fine.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of operating an adult arcade without a permit and assessed a fine. The lower court affirmed appellant's conviction and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Houston, Tex., Ordinance 85-1337 was not void under Tex. Const. art. XI, § 5 because the ordinance did not invade the state law-making function because it had a different purpose than Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 8814 and 8817 (Vernon 1964). The ordinance was to discourage adult arcades as places of sexual encounter or solicitation and arts. 8814 and 8817 were to provide comprehensive regulation of music and skill or pleasure coin-operated machines. The court held that Houston, Tex., Ordinance 28.849(b) was not in conflict with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372w because the ordinance required proof of interior design compliance to discourage the use of an adult arcade as place for sexual encounters, while the permit in art. 2372 was enacted to ensure an upgrading of residential business neighborhoods and to prevent crime in those areas. Absent a direct conflict, the court was required to harmonize different statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision, which affirmed appellant's conviction of operating an adult arcade without a permit and assessed a fine because the municipal ordinances were not void and unconstitutional because they did not conflict with related state laws.

 

836 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Koury v. State


No. 01-87-01088-CR,


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1787



July 28, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 964,934


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence, entered by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County (Texas), upon a plea of nolo contendere, asserting trial court error in overruling a motion to quash the information, unconstitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1)(A), and insufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced for the misdemeanor offense of obscenity after he pleaded nolo contendere to the charge. Defendant appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to quash the information. He claimed that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.31(a)(1)(A) was unconstitutional, and that the evidence was insufficient because the state had failed to obtain a prior adjudication that the magazine was obscene. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that defendant did not enumerate how § 42.31(a)(1)(A) was unconstitutional, and that prior decisions had found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that it was without jurisdiction to consider whether the trial court erred by not obtaining a prior adjudication that the magazine was obscene, because defendant had not urged this contention in his motion to quash, and had pleaded nolo contendere to the charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that defendant was properly sentenced for the misdemeanor offense of obscenity after his plea of nolo contendere. The court held that the obscenity statute was not unconstitutionally vague, and found that it was without jurisdiction to consider whether the evidence was sufficient because defendant had not raised the issue in his motion to quash or in his plea.

 

837 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 01-87-00463-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1798



July 28, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 464,728


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his criminal conviction for burglary of a motor vehicle from the 335th District Court, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted of burglary of a motor vehicle. At sentencing, the jury found two enhancement paragraphs to be true. Defendant asserted on appeal that the punishment charge required reversal because it required a minimum sentence of 25 years due to the enhancement paragraphs. The court affirmed the conviction. Although the charge was mandatory and constitutional, defendant did not object, so the issue was not preserved for review. Defendant also complained that the trial court gave an unconstitutional jury charge regarding the consideration of parole. Since the instruction made no contribution to the punishment, the court overruled that point of error. Defendant also argued that the trial judge did not have jurisdiction, as he was assigned to the case contrary to Tex. Gov't Code Ann § 74.061. However, defendant did not object to the judicial assignment at trial. Thus, the error was not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant, finding that defendant failed to object to a judicial assignment and to enhancement paragraphs. Further, an allegedly improper jury charge regarding parole had no effect on the outcome of the case.

 

838 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Chambers v. State


No. 01-86-00520-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


755 S.W.2d 907; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1807



July 28, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 230th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 444,833.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the 230th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which found him guilty of indecency with a child, and assessed his punishment at 16-1/2 years of confinement.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution offered a videotape of the complainant to prove the alleged crime. Defendant called the complainant as a witness and she denied that the crime occurred. The only eyewitnesses to the alleged crime were defendant and the complainant. There was no medical evidence establishing that defendant was engaged in sexual activity with the complainant. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction and acquitted defendant, holding that defendant's guilt was not proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found the only evidence of guilt against defendant was the videotape that was an ex parte, out-of-court statement, without oath, confrontation or notice, which the complainant then repudiated at trial. Only by disregarding all sworn testimony from eyewitnesses could the jury have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant exposed his genitals to the complainant as alleged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction and entered a judgment of acquittal for defendant because the only evidence of the alleged crime was a videotape of the complainant, which she repudiated at trial when she denied that the crime occurred.

 

839 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Zwack v. State


No. A14-87-00427-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


757 S.W.2d 66; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1808



July 28, 1988, Decided  
July 28, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 05/10/1989
Post-conviction relief denied at Zwack v. Texas, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 30012 (S.D. Tex., Mar. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 442,893.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, which entered a judgment of conviction for capital murder of a peace officer, and refused to permit defense counsel to read portions of a learned treatise into evidence under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 803(18), denied an instruction on self-defense, and permitted instruction on parole laws.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder of a peace officer after alleging that he had an insane delusion that police were ambushing him. The trial court denied admission of a learned treatise on insanity, refused an instruction on self-defense based on delusion, and permitted an instruction on parole laws. The court affirmed the conviction because there was no prejudicial error by the trial court. The court found that the learned treatise was not introduced in conjunction with expert testimony and thus was inadmissible under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 803(18). The court further found that Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 46.03 § 1(e) (1988) was constitutional because statutes prescribing the disposition of guilt by reason of insanity were the province of the court and not the jury, and thus the jury was prohibited from instruction. The self-defense instruction was correctly disallowed because the circumstances as perceived by defendant did not constitute a defense for the use of deadly force, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 9.31, 9.32 (1974). Although instructions on parole laws were improper, there was no evidence that this information contributed to the punishment assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder of a peace officer because the trial court correctly disallowed learned treatise evidence on insanity, and further found that defendant was not entitled to a self-defense instruction, because the circumstances did not constitute such a defense. The court found that even though the jury was improperly instructed on parole laws, it made no contribution to the sentence.

 

840 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Castillo v. State


No. 01-88-00066-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1813



July 28, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 963,478


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9 of Harris County, Texas, which convicted her of misdemeanor possession of obscene material with the intent to sell, alleging that the statute upon which the information was based was indefinite, uncertain, and vague and that there was not a timely and proper determination of obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of misdemeanor possession of obscene material with the intent to sell. Defendant alleged generally that the Texas Obscenity Statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 (1988) was unconstitutionally vague and that the trial court erred in denying her pretrial motion to quash the indictment because there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, holding that defendant failed to cite to any specific language contained in § 43.21 which was indefinite, vague, or uncertain, and § 43.21 had been held to be otherwise constitutional, therefore the court would not engage in a search for unconstitutionality. The court also rejected defendant's allegation that the trial court erred in denying her pretrial motion to quash the indictment based on the fact that there was no timely and proper determination of obscenity because the court had previously rejected that contention in another opinion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of misdemeanor possession of obscene material with the intent to sell, holding that the court would not engage in a search for unconstitutionality where defendant failed to cite to any specific language contained in the statute which was indefinite, vague, or uncertain.

Bobo v. State


Nos. B14-87-00362-CR, B14-87-00363-CR, B14-87-00364-CR, B14-87-00365-CR, B14-87-00366-CR, B14-87-00367-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


757 S.W.2d 58; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1822



July 28, 1988, Decided  
July 28, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 912,864; 912,866; 912,861; 912,862; 912,863; & 912,857.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for misdemeanor criminal trespass by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5, Harris County (Texas) on the ground the informations did not allege offenses. Defendants contended that they were denied their defenses of necessity and defense of a third person, that evidence relevant to those defenses was improperly excluded, that the state's argument was prejudicial, and that probation conditions were improper.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of misdemeanor criminal trespass under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 for their activities at an abortion clinic. The court affirmed and held that the indictment alleged the essential elements and gave proper notice under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 21.17 (1966). The court held that defendants were not deprived of a fair trial or due process because they could not meet all the elements of the claimed defense of necessity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 9.22, or the defense of a third person under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 9.33, or establish relevance for the excluded evidence on abortion because the unborn were not persons for purposes of U.S. Const. amend. XIV protection. The court found that the prosecutor properly used a chart to summarize evidence and that his improper remark about defense counsel was not harmful to defendants. The court upheld the denial of a defendant's motion for an instructed verdict because the defendant waived any error by putting on a defense after the state rested. The court modified the probation order because the limitation on defendants' right to picket and demonstrate was outside the scope of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 42.12.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions because the indictments alleged the essential elements, defendants failed to meet the elements of their defenses, and related evidence was properly excluded as irrelevant. The court found that the state's use of a chart during summation was proper and that the prosecutor's improper remark was not harmful. The court modified the terms of probation because picketing and protesting did not violate the law.

Garcia v. State


No. 01-87-00688-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1725



July 21, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 439,579


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment entered by the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him after he pled guilty to solicitation of capital murder, and sentenced him to five years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea bargain, appellant pled guilty and was convicted of solicitation to commit capital murder. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and found that the trial court did not err when it overruled appellant's motion to quash the indictment because the grand jury did not prepare a memorandum pursuant to Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 20.19 (1977). The court determined that art. 20.19 was directory rather than mandatory. The court also rejected appellant's interpretation of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977), which appellant contended on three points of error was unconstitutional. The court found that art. 1.15 was constitutional and did not prohibit appellant from presenting evidence at the punishment hearing. The court further found that appellant was not denied the right to a fair trial or the right to compulsory process because of art. 1.15.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the grand jury's failure to prepare a memorandum required by statute was not reversible error. Further, a statute that provided for a bench trial following appellant's plea of guilty was not unconstitutional because it did not deny appellant from offering evidence at sentencing, and it did not violate appellant's rights to jury trial and compulsory process.
