Jones v. State


No. C14-87-00510-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


756 S.W.2d 376; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1731



July 21, 1988, Decided  
July 21, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11 Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 937,470.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11, Harris County, Texas, which found him guilty of the misdemeanor offense of carrying a weapon after his conviction by a jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress oral statements that he made after his arrest under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22 (1979). He also argued that the prosecutor's peremptory challenge of all black persons on the panel violated his equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found no evidence that the state engaged in unconstitutional purposeful discrimination through its use of peremptory challenges. At the Batson hearing on defendant's motion, the trial court found that defendant raised an inference of discrimination on the part of the state. However, the trial court also found that the state provided racially neutral explanations for the strikes, and that defendant failed to carry his burden rebutting the state's explanations. The court found that defendant's statements to police, that he had not fired the pistol because there was a spent round under the hammer, indicated his familiarity with and control over the pistol and tended to establish his guilt. The statement was admissible under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22 § 3(c) (1979).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found defendant guilty of the misdemeanor offense of carrying a weapon because defendant did not satisfy his burden of rebutting the state's racially neutral explanations for the peremptory strikes, and that the statements defendant made to police were admissible.

Thomas v. State


No. B14-87-00065-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1755



July 21, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 451,015


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of indecency with a child, based on Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 21.01(2), 21.11(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found lying on top of autistic child who could not dress herself and could not speak by the child's brother. Defendant tried to coerce the child's brother into not telling his mother what he had seen by reminding him of the things defendant had bought him. Defendant was convicted of indecency with a child pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 21.01(2), 21.11(a)(1). Defendant sought review of his conviction, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence. Penal Code Ann. § 21.01(2). The court also held that any reasonable trier of fact could infer from the evidence of defendant's conduct observed in the bedroom, and his remarks to the child's brother, that he had acted with intent to arouse or gratify his sexual desires, constituting the requisite specific intent under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, finding that there was sufficient evidence such that any reasonable trier of fact could have found the essential elements of indecency with a child beyond a reasonable doubt.

Barnes v. J.W. Bateson Co.

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 48TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, airport employee and airline, challenged the judgment of the 48th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), granting summary judgment in favor of appellees, architectural firm, electrical subcontractor, and general contractors, in an action arising from personal injuries to appellant airport employee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant airport employee filed an action for personal injuries against appellant airline and appellees, architectural firm, electrical subcontractor, and general contractors. Appellant airline cross-claimed for contribution and indemnity against appellees. On appeal, the court affirmed the grant of appellees' motions for summary judgment on the grounds appellants' claims were barred by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. 847 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Raborn


No. 01-87-00193-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


754 S.W.2d 481; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1665



July 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 310th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-45725.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of a turnover order of the 310th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which was entered to satisfy a money judgment previously rendered in favor of appellee creditor.


OVERVIEW: Under a turnover order, appellant debtor was required to endorse and turn over to a court-appointed receiver all income, including all salary checks, received from his employer, in order to satisfy a judgment in favor of appellee creditor. Appellant was required to continue to turn over such income as it was received. The reviewing court overturned the order. A trial court only has the authority under the turnover statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 31.002 (1986), to order a judgment debtor to turn over checks, evidencing wages, when such checks are collected and in the possession or in the control of the debtor. Under the turnover statute, a trial court is not empowered to order a judgment debtor to turn over exempt property. Thus, a trial court can order wages turned over to a receiver only after the wages are paid to and received by the debtor, whether by check or in cash.


OUTCOME: A turnover order that was entered to satisfy a money judgment previously rendered against appellant debtor in favor of appellee creditor was reversed and remanded because under the turnover statute the trial court was not empowered to order a judgment debtor to turn over future wages.

Roberts v. State


Appeal No. 04-87-00631-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


754 S.W.2d 477; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2118



July 13, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the County Court at Law of Medina County, Trial Court No. 109-ED, Honorable Joe E. Briscoe, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condemnees sought review of a judgment for the state from the County Court at Law of Medina County (Texas), contending that the trial court erred in its instruction to the jury regarding the determination of the land.


OVERVIEW: In a condemnation case, the trial court instructed the jury that in arriving at the value of appellant condemnees' land that was taken by the state not to consider any enhancement or damages to the value of the remaining land. Thereafter, the trial court entered a judgment adverse to appellants upon the jury's verdict. Appellants sought review, arguing that the instruction constituted reversible error. The court agreed with appellants, reversed the decision, and remanded for a new trial. The court found a need for special instructions to the jury because of the confusing evidence Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 21.042(e), which was declared unconstitutional after the trial court proceeding. Further, the appraisal theory advanced by the state, condemned by a Texas Supreme Court decision, and encouraged by the unconstitutional statute, led to the inescapable conclusion that such appraisal resulted in offsetting the estimated enhanced value of the remainder after the condemnation against the market value of the part taken at the time of the condemnation. Accordingly, the jury answers suggested the same conclusion, which would have been cured by appellants' requested instruction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for the state and remanded the cause to the trial court, holding that the trial court committed reversible error by instructing the jury, that in arriving at the value of appellant condemnees' land that was taken by the state, not to consider any enhancement or damages to the value of the remaining land.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated, holding that the indictment was sufficient, the trial court did not err in the admission of testimony, and appellant was not entitled to a mistrial.

White v. State


Nos. 01-87-01030-CR, 01-87-01031-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1518



June 30, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 964,959; 967,729


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12 of Harris County (Texas) finding him guilty, pursuant to a plea bargain, of two counts of possessing obscene devices with intent to sell them.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled nolo contendere, pursuant to a plea bargain agreement, to two counts of possessing obscene devices with intent to sell them. Appellant was found guilty and then sought review of the trial court's order arguing that the trial court erred in overruling his pretrial motion to quash, because (1) the statute upon which the information was based is unconstitutionally indefinite, uncertain, and vague, and (2) there was not "a timely and proper determination of obscenity." The court found that appellant could not point to a specific provision of the statute that was vague but rather argued in general terms that criminal statutes penalizing "pure speech" should be subject to the most rigorous scrutiny. The court noted that obscene devises are not considered "pure speech" and noted that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 (Supp. 1988) had withstood numerous challenges on the same grounds. With respect to appellant's second point of error, the court found that appellant had failed to raise the point in a pretrial motion to quash and, because appellant's conviction was based on a plea bargain, appellant was precluded from raising the issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and conviction of the trial court.

 

853 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. State


No. 01-87-00369-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


755 S.W.2d 505; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1559



June 30, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 467,844.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), for delivery of more than 50 pounds and less than 200 pounds of marijuana, contending that there were errors in the jury charge and the prosecution's argument to the jury that deprived him of a fair trial and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of delivery of more than 50 pounds and less than 200 pounds of marijuana, and assessed his punishment at 25 years confinement and a fine. Appellant complained that the prosecution's argument included references to the quantity and value of the marijuana, the low pay of the officers who testified, importance of the case to the county, the large numbers of "dope dealers" in the county, the problem of the availability of "dope" to school children, and the fact that the jury had already acquitted one "dope dealer" in this case, all of which was outside the record. The court concluded that there was a reasonable possibility that the improper argument contributed to the punishment assessed, and sustained this point of error. The court also sustained appellant's contention with regard to error in the jury instruction on parole law. The court overruled appellant's contention that trial counsel's representation was defective, finding no reasonable probability that the result of the proceeding at the guilt/innocence stage would have been different. The court affirmed on the issue of appellant's guilt, but reversed at the punishment stage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court on the issue of appellant's guilt. However, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court at the punishment stage and remanded for a new punishment hearing on the grounds that the court could not say beyond a reasonable doubt that the various errors below made no contribution to the punishment.

 

854 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Santikos v. State


No. 13-87-393-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


754 S.W.2d 416; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1600



June 30, 1988, Decided  
June 30, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted January 17, 1990.
Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Granted June 3, 1992. Prior Opinion Withdrawn June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 24th District Court of Victoria County, Texas. TR. CT. NO. 86-8-12,478.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for possession of cocaine from the 24th District Court of Victoria County (Texas), arguing that an inspection for violations of the Texas Alcoholic Beverage Code was a subterfuge or pretext to discover a violation of the Controlled Substance Act and challenging the constitutionality of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 101.04 (1978)and 104.01(9) (Supp. 1988).


OVERVIEW: After receiving a complaint concerning narcotics activities on the premises of a nightclub, agents of the Alcoholic Beverage Commission (Texas) obtained appellant's consent to search a filing cabinet where they discovered cocaine. Upon a plea of nolo contendere, the trial court convicted appellant of possession of cocaine. Appellant sought review of the decision, arguing that the search was a subterfuge or pretext and challenging the constitutionality of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 101.04 (1978) and 104.01(9) (Supp. 1988). The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the trial court properly overruled appellant's motion to suppress because appellant voluntarily consented to the search that resulted in the seizure. Further, the court upheld the constitutionality of the challenged statutes. Section § 101.04, which authorized an inspection of a licensed establishment at any time, did not authorize unreasonable searches. Finally, § 104.01(9), which authorized the commission to investigate a licensed premises for the presence of narcotics or equipment used for administering narcotics, was narrowly limited and did not authorize searches of any criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of cocaine, holding that appellant voluntarily consented to the search and upholding the constitutionality of statutes authorizing the inspection of licensed establishments at any time and investigation of licensed premises for the presence of narcotics or equipment used for administering narcotics.

Zimmerman v. State


No. 13-87-154-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


754 S.W.2d 402; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1676



June 30, 1988, Decided  
June 30, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Refused


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 214th District Court of Neuces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 214th District Court of Neuces County (Texas), in which he was convicted of burglary of a habitation and sentenced to life in prison plus a monetary fine.


OVERVIEW: On review, appellant contended that his conviction had been inappropriate because the trial court had erred in overruling appellant's special plea in bar based on collateral estoppel. The appellate court found that because the verdict of acquittal in the former prosecution for aggravated sexual assault could have been based on an issue other than entry, the issue of whether appellant entered the victim's home was properly relitigated. The appellate court accordingly held that collateral estoppel did not bar the instant prosecution and overruled that point of error. The appellate court then found that it was not error for the trial court to admit into evidence a two-page parole certificate and that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's affirmative finding that appellant used a deadly weapon during the commission of the burglary offense. The appellate court affirmed, concluding that the parole law charge given pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (Supp. 1988) did not constitute reversible error where it failed to make a contribution to the jury's assessment of sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence, finding that the trial court properly overruled appellant's special plea in bar based on collateral estoppel from a prior acquittal in an aggravated sexual assault case. The issue of whether appellant had entered the victim's home was properly relitigated in the instant prosecution where the verdict on the assault charge could have been based on an issue other than entry.

Silva v. State


Nos. 01-87-00756-CR, 01-87-00757-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1677



June 30, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 945,685, 948,722


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from judgment of County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him, upon his nolo contendere plea pursuant to plea bargain, of two charges of selling obscene materials in violation of Texas Obscenity Statute, Texas Penal Code ch. 43, subch. B (1988).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea bargain, appellant pleaded nolo contendere to two charges of selling obscene materials in violation of the Texas Obscenity Statute, Texas Penal Code ch. 43, subch. B (1988). The court affirmed his convictions. It rejected appellant's claim that the statute violated U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV. Appellant failed to enumerate a specific example of how the statute operated against him, or in general, in an unconstitutional fashion. Further, Texas courts of appeal had found Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a) to be constitutional. The court rejected appellant's contention that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions because the state failed to obtain a judicial determination that the material at issue was statutorily obscene. Appellant pleaded nolo contendere pursuant to plea bargain, the terms of which were followed by the trial court. Appellant did not raise this particular argument in his pretrial motions to quash, nor did he obtain the trial court's permission to argue so on appeal. Thus, the court was jurisdictionally unable to address appellant's argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions, holding appellant, by his failure to enumerate any example of an unconstitutional application, had failed to rebut the presumption that the Texas Obscenity Statute was constitutional. Appellant waived his challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence to support his convictions by pleading nolo contendere.

Franklin v. Wheeless


No. A14-86-00802-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1679



June 30, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 152nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 79-3926


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of an order from the 152nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which rendered a take nothing judgment to appellant in her action against appellees doctor and drug company for damages pertaining to appellees' alleged failure to inform appellant of side effects of drug treatment for psoriasis.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient obtained treatment for psoriasis from appellee doctor. Appellee doctor failed to inform appellant of the potential side effects of medication made by appellee drug company, which appellee doctor used to treat appellant. The medication helped appellant, but she suffered from some of the side effects. Appellant filed an action against appellees for negligence in failing to disclose the side effects. At trial, the jury found that appellee doctor had failed to disclose the risks of using the medication, but that the failure did not constitute negligence, that appellee drug company adequately disclosed the risks, and that a reasonable person would not have refused the medication had the risks been disclose. As a result, the trial court entered a take nothing judgment, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed and held that the jury's findings were not against the great weight and preponderance of the evidence, that there was no trial error in the jury instructions, and that the evidence did not establish an award of damages as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's take nothing judgment because it found that the jury's findings were not against the great weight of the evidence and that the evidence did not establish a damage award.

 

858 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lloyd v. State


No. 01-87-00608-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1681



June 30, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 479,919


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the judgment of the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of burglary of a building and sentenced him to 65 years confinement after he stole an all-terrain vehicle from a dealership.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary of a building and sentenced to 65 years confinement after he stole an all-terrain vehicle from a dealership. The court affirmed his conviction. While the trial judge gave the jury a statutory parole charge that had since been held unconstitutional, it was not necessary to reverse appellant's conviction because the error made no contribution to his punishment. The minimum sentence for the offense was 25 years, the trial judge gave a curative instruction to the jury as to what they could and could not consider with respect to the parole laws, and the state submitted evidence of appellant's prior criminal record, which included five prior felony convictions. There was sufficient evidence to establish that the dealership was a "building" within the definition of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.01(2) (1974). That statute defined "building" as any enclosed structure intended for use or occupation as a habitation or for some purpose of trade, manufacture, ornament, or use. The uncontradicted evidence showed that glass was broken to gain entry to the dealership and there was consistent unobjected to testimony during trial that the premises was a building.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that, while trial judge gave jury a statutory parole charge that was held unconstitutional, it was not necessary to reverse conviction because error made no contribution to his punishment. There was sufficient evidence to establish that dealership was a building for purposes of burglary statute.

Walker v. Employees Retirement System


No. 3-87-157-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


753 S.W.2d 796; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1941



June 29, 1988, Decided  
June 29, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing overruled August 10, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 383,228, HONORABLE JERRY DELLANA, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), which affirmed appellee retirement system's decision to deny appellant an additional retirement annuity under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 110B, § 44.102(b) because he did not retire within the time proscribed for the incentive benefit.


OVERVIEW: Appellee retirement system denied appellant judge an additional retirement annuity under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 110B, § 44.102(b) because he did not retire within the time proscribed for the incentive benefit. The district court affirmed appellee's decision. The court affirmed the district court's decision and held that because appellant did not retire immediately upon becoming eligible or before reaching age 71, he was not entitled to the additional benefits provided in § 44.102(b). The court held that § 44.102(b) encouraged and compensated voluntary retirement at an age within the constitutionally mandated range between age 70 and age 75. The court held that it reasonably fit within the general purpose of the Judicial Retirement System to have established a program of benefits and was not a violation of appellant's equal protection rights against being discriminated on the basis of age. The court held that even if appellant had been correct in his constitutional attack, the result would not have been to increase his retirement, but instead the base retirement pay provision found elsewhere in the statute would have controlled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellee retirement system's judgment that denied appellant judge an additional retirement annuity because he did not retire within the time proscribed for the incentive benefit. Statute was not unconstitutional and did not violate equal protection because it reasonably fit within the general purpose of the Judicial Retirement System to have established a program of benefits.

De Luna v. Rizkallah


No. 01-87-00906-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


754 S.W.2d 366; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1466



June 23, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 189th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-59229-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient and patient's husband, challenged the grant of summary judgment for appellee physician in the 189th District Court, Harris County, Texas in appellants' medical malpractice suit against appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, patient and patient's husband, filed a medical malpractice suit against appellee physician based on appellee's erroneous interpretation of two echocardiograms. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellee based on a finding that appellants' cause of action was barred as a matter of law by the applicable statute of limitations. Appellants challenged. The court found that the evidence submitted by appellants in opposition to appellee's motion for summary judgment conclusively showed that they could not have discovered the wrong within two years of appellant patient's last treatment from appellee. Thus, based upon the decisions of other cases, the court held that the absolute two-year statute of limitation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, §10.01 (1987) was unconstitutional as applied to appellants' cause of action because it violated the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, §13. Accordingly, the summary judgment was reversed and the cause remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment for appellee physician in appellants, patient and patient's husband's, medical malpractice suit and remanded the cause for further proceedings because appellants could not have discovered the wrong within two years. Thus, the absolute two-year statute of limitation was unconstitutional, as applied to appellants.

Wishnow v. Texas Alcoholic Beverage Com.


No. B14-87-00893-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


757 S.W.2d 404; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1475



June 23, 1988, Decided  
June 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 129th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 87-38279.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club owner challenged the judgment of the 129th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which affirmed the order of appellee Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission's 60-day suspension of appellant's mixed beverage and late hours permit.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing, appellee Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission suspended appellant club owner's mixed beverage and late hours permits for a period of 60 days. Appellee determined that appellant, through his patrons and employees, had violated Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 11.61(b)(7) and 104.01(2), as well as Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 21.01. 21.07, 21.08, and §§ 4.03(a) and 4.04(a) of the Controlled Substances Act. The district court affirmed the suspension. Appellant challenged that decision. On appeal, the court affirmed. Applying the fair notice test in its constitutional analysis of §§ 11.61(b)(7) and 104.01(2), which were regulatory statutes governing business activity, the court held that the statutes were not vague. Also, § 21.01 and § 21.07 were not vague. The court held that sufficient evidence supported the conclusion that appellant knew or should have known that prohibited conduct was occurring on the premises, which included the sidewalk outside the club. The fact that appellee was aware of the prohibited conduct when it previously renewed appellant's permits, did not render evidence of such prohibited conduct inadmissible at the suspension hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment affirming appellee Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission's order suspending appellant club owner's mixed beverage and late hours permits for 60 days. The statutory provisions upon which the suspension was based provided appellant with fair notice of the conduct prohibited. Sufficient evidence showed that appellant knew or should have know that the prohibited conduct was occurring on club premises.

Miller v. State


No. 01-87-00554-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


753 S.W.2d 473; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1494



June 23, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 262nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 326,456.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 262nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in an altercation with the victim. During the altercation, the victim was shot and killed by defendant. Defendant was subsequently convicted of murder for the death of the victim. Defendant challenged his conviction and claimed that the lower court erred when it refused to instruct the jury on the lesser charge of involuntary manslaughter because the shot occurred as a result of sudden passion. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because there was no evidence that warranted an instruction on involuntary manslaughter. The court held that the lower court's use of the word "murder" in the charge to the jury did not constitute a harmful comment on the weight of the evidence. The court also held that the exclusion of a defense witness, although erroneous, did not amount to harmful error because there was sufficient evidence that defendant had threatened the victim with bodily harm. The court reformed the judgment to delete the jury's answer to the deadly weapon special issue because the state failed to give proper notice of its intention to submit the finding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction because there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction and a lack of evidence to support the jury charge on the lesser charge of involuntary manslaughter. The court reformed the judgment to the extent that it deleted the jury's answer to the deadly weapon special issue because the state failed to give proper notice.

Fambro v. State


No. 11-87-257-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


751 S.W.2d 956; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3425



June 23, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Comanche County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in Comanche County (Texas) for burglary of a building, contending that the trial court erred in failing to instruct a verdict of not guilty because the evidence was insufficient to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and in charging the jury regarding parole laws over timely objection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for burglary of a building, contending that the trial court erred in failing to instruct a verdict of not guilty because the evidence was insufficient to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and in charging the jury regarding parole laws over timely objection. The court affirmed and held that the faulty parole instruction made no contribution to the 12-year punishment which was assessed by the jury. Even presuming that the jury followed the trial court's faulty instruction not to consider the manner in which the parole laws could have been applied to this particular defendant, the jury not only rejected appellant's sworn testimony during trial, but they were also aware of his prior convictions for burglary of a building and felony driving while intoxicated. Consequently, the court held that error was "harmless error" under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2). The court overruled defendant's objection as to the sufficiency of the evidence because defendant was in possession of recently stolen property at the time of his arrest, and the jury was not required to accept his claim that he had bought all of this property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary of a building because the faulty parole instruction made no contribution to the 12-year punishment which was assessed by the jury, and was thus a harmless error, and the evidence was sufficient because the jury was not required to accept his claim that he had bought all of the stolen property found in his possession at the time of his arrest.

Urbano v. State


No. 01-87-00674-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1406



June 16, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Opinion on Rehearing August 25, 1988; Withdrawn and Substituted August 25, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 466,775, William T. Harmon, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 178th District Court of Harris County (Texas), that found him guilty of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 99 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery. In his first point of error, appellant contended that the trial court erred in granting the state's motion to shuffle the names of the jury panel because the venire had already been shuffled once. In his second point of error, appellant contended that the court erred in shuffling without notice to either appellant or his counsel, as well as doing so outside of their presence. In his third point of error, appellant contended that the prosecutor committed reversible error by discussing victims' rights during argument at the punishment phase of the trial, and by asking the jury to punish appellant because of the existence, and possible exercise, of his constitutional rights. In his fourth point of error, appellant contended that the court erred in charging the jury on the law of parole. After review, the court overruled appellant's first three points of error. As to the fourth point of error, appellant was harmed by the court's instruction, so the judgment was reversed as to the verdict of punishment and remanded to the trial court for a new trial on punishment. Otherwise, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that found appellant guilty of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 99 years was reversed and remanded for a new trial on the matter of punishment because appellant was harmed as a result of the court's instruction on the law of parole. The judgment was otherwise affirmed because the court did not err in shuffling the juror's names and the prosecutor did not make an improper remark during the punishment phase.

 

867 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Eason v. State


No. 01-87-00233-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1543



June 16, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On Motion For Rehearing opinion Withdrawn and Substituted July 28, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 469,008


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment, based on a jury verdict, by the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of attempted murder and assessed punishment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempted murder after he allegedly stabbed the victim in the back. On appeal, the court affirmed after it reformed the judgment to delete the recitation of the jury's answer to the deadly weapon special issue, and the trial court's affirmative finding on that issue, because appellant did not have sufficient notice. The state had to provide in its pleadings its intention to seek a deadly weapon finding and give likewise notice when it decided not to proceed on such a finding. There was sufficient testimonial evidence to support the jury's findings that appellant did not act in self-defense. The state's misstatement of testimony was not manifestly improper. There was no evidence in the record that a memorandum was not prepared prior to the preparation of the indictment to support appellant's motion to quash the indictment. Although a jury charge on the parole law was unconstitutional, reversal was not required because there was no egregious harm to appellant given the totality of the evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reformed to delete the recitation of the jury's answer to the deadly weapons special issue, as well as the trial court's affirmative findings on that issue, and affirmed. The state failed to give required notice to appellant when it decided it would not proceed on the deadly weapons special issue. There was no egregious harm to appellant in the trial court's unconstitutional parole law jury charge.

 

868 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cedar Crest #10, Inc. v. Dallas


No. 11-87-112-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


754 S.W.2d 351; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2043



June 16, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of May 19, 1988, Reported at 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1090.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Dallas County. Opinion of May 19, 1988 withdrawn and substituted. Reported at 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1090.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, apartment building owner, challenged the judgment of the District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which affirmed the administrative decision of the Urban Rehabilitation Standards Board that ruled in favor of appellee city and declared appellant's building to be a nuisance and ordered its demolition pursuant to Dallas City Code § 27 (1960).


OVERVIEW: Appellee city, through the Urban Rehabilitation Standards Board (Board), found that the vacant building owned by appellant, apartment building owner, was a public nuisance and ordered its demolition. Appellant challenged the Board's decision in the district court pursuant to Dallas City Code § 27-9(e) (1960), which permitted only a limited judicial review hearing under the substantial evidence rule. On appeal, the court held that the ordinance did not violate appellant's constitutional guarantee of due process because adequate safeguards in the notices, hearings, and opportunities for compliance were provided. Appellant also contended that there was no trial on the merits and no factual evidence to support the Board's findings. There were no factual findings in the record, and the court had little basis for review and presumed that the evidence supported the judgment of the district court. Finally, the court held that appellee's action was not barred by estoppel because appellee's assertion that the building was a nuisance under Dallas City Code § 16 (1960) did not judicially estop appellee from asserting that the building was a nuisance under Dallas City Code § 27 (1960).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court. The district court held that the city ordinance, which provided for a limited judicial review after an administrative decision to declare a building a nuisance and order its demolition, did not violate appellant apartment building owner's rights to due process of law.

 

869 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Watauga v. Taylor


No. 2-87-160-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


752 S.W.2d 199; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1581



June 8, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 67TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the 67th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), that awarded appellee property owners $ 3,000 for damages to their home, $ 6,800 for destruction of fixtures and personal property, $ 19,500 for mental anguish, and $ 15,000 for attorneys' fees for damages to real and personal property resulting from the flooding of appellees' home which was adjacent to drainage ditches maintained by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owners brought suit against appellant city for damages to real and personal property caused by the flooding of their home which lay adjacent to drainage ditches maintained by appellant. The trial court awarded appellees $ 3,000 for damages to their home, $ 6,800 for destruction to personal property, $ 19,500 for mental anguish, and $ 15,000 for attorneys' fees. Appellant challenged the basis for the awards except that for property damage, arguing that it was protected under the doctrine of governmental immunity. Here, evidence indicated that appellant negligently maintained a storm sewer, and was liable because such an act was ministerial in nature and could be performed by a private subcontractor. The court found that the testimony of only one appellee established injuries sufficient to constitute negligent infliction of emotional distress. Unless attorneys' fees were provided by statute or by contract, such fees were not recoverable in a tort action. Texas courts held negligently destroying property was not a taking of property. Therefore, appellees were not entitled to such fees and the court affirmed the trial court's decision in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that awarded property damages to appellee property owners where appellant city negligently maintained a storm sewer and was not protected by governmental immunity. It reversed an award of attorneys' fees where no statutory or contract basis was provided and reversed an award for damages for the negligent infliction of emotional distress where appellee's testimony failed to establish sufficient injury.

 

870 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lear v. State


Nos. 3-87-084-CR, 3-87-085-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


753 S.W.2d 737; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1954



June 8, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF TRAVIS COUNTY, NOS. 253,805 AND 254,331, HONORABLE LESLIE D. TAYLOR, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 1 of Travis County (Texas), which found her guilty on two charges of harboring a barking dog under Austin, Tex., Code § 3-3-9, violation of which was a class "C" misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's seven dogs' barking so disturbed defendant's neighbors that they had moved out of the bedroom that was located in closest proximity to defendant's house. On two occasions after that, defendant's dogs barked constantly for extended periods in the middle of the night, awakening the neighbors. The neighbors never had problems sleeping until the problem with defendant's dogs began. Defendant was convicted on two charges of harboring a barking dog under Austin, Tex., Code § 3-3-9, violation of which was a class "C" misdemeanor. The court affirmed the convictions. Austin, Tex., Code § 3-3-9 was not unconstitutionally vague because it did not reach constitutionally protected conduct. The words used in the standard of conduct proscribed by section 3-3-9, when given their plain ordinary dictionary meanings, were understandable by a person of ordinary intelligence. Accordingly, defendant had fair warning on the nature of the conduct that violated the section.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding defendant guilty on two charges of harboring a barking dog under Austin, Tex., Code § 3-3-9 was affirmed. The city code section under which defendant was convicted was not so vague and overbroad that it violated due process of law under both the Fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution and the Texas Constitution.

 

871 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Graham v. Hutchinson County Appraisal Review Bd.


No. 07-87-0202-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


776 S.W.2d 592; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 3431



June 6, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HUTCHINSON COUNTY; 84TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. 14,335; HONORABLE J.E. BLACKBURN, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Hutchinson County, 84th Judicial District (Texas) that dismissed their property tax protest for lack of jurisdiction, on grounds that compliance with Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.08 (1988) was unnecessary to invoke jurisdiction, appellee board's and appellee director's pleas to jurisdiction were defective, and that Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.09 (1982) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers sued appellee board and appellee directors, claiming that their property appraisals were inequitable. Appellants sought review after the lower court dismissed the suit for lack of jurisdiction. The court found that appellants did not properly preserve their appeal under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.08 (1988) because they paid their property taxes for the year they were claiming inequitable appraisal. Under § 42.08, appellants could have paid the prior year's tax, paid taxes based on an independent appraisal, or paid taxes based on what they considered the proper property appraisal. Appellants did not preserve for review their claim that affidavits supporting appellees' pleas to the jurisdiction were defective. Appellants also claimed that Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.09 (1982) was unconstitutional because it limited the ways they could appeal appraisals. Appellants' federal and state due process rights were not violated by § 42.09 because they were given the opportunity to be heard on the assessment before the valuation was finally determined and had availed themselves of all available administrative remedies and procedures. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing appellant taxpayers' suit against appellee board and appellee director protesting inequitable property appraisals was affirmed. Appellants did not comply with statutorily mandated procedures to preserve their protest when they paid their disputed property taxes in full. The statutory procedures for protesting appraisals did not unconstitutionally limit their due process rights because they had opportunities to be heard.

Ford v. State


No. 01-87-01126-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


753 S.W.2d 451; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1232



June 2, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 963,477.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County (Texas), where appellant was convicted of selling obscene materials.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of selling obscene materials following a plea bargain with the state. On review, appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying her motion to quash because Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43.21 was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. First, the court held that a statute was presumed to be constitutional. The court stated that the Texas Court of Criminal Appeals had held that article 43.21(a)(1)(A) was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that appellant failed to rebut the presumption of constitutionality. Next, the court held that it lacked jurisdiction to consider appellant's argument that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction and that article 43.21(a)(1)(A) was unconstitutional based on new law because appellant failed to seek the trial court's permission to argue so on appeal. Lastly, the court held that article 43.21(a)(1)(A) complied with the law in that it incorporated the correct standard for determining whether a piece of work had any value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for selling obscene materials because appellant failed to specify how the statute was unconstitutionally vague, as such, appellant failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality.

Jenkins v. State

OVERVIEW: Appellant pled nolo contendere and was found guilty of selling obscene materials and sought review of the trial court's denial of her motion to quash. Childress v. State


No. 01-87-01090-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 941; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1260



June 2, 1988, Decided  
June 2, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law #7, Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 959,390.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the County Court at Law # 7 of Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of selling obscene material. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motion to quash the indictment because the Texas Obscenity Statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 (1998), was allegedly unconstitutionally vague and therefore void.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted, following his plea of nolo contendere, of selling obscene material. Appellant argued on appeal that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motion to quash the indictment because the Texas Obscenity Statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 (1998), was allegedly unconstitutionally vague and therefore void. Appellant also argued that § 43.21 contravened U.S. Const. amend. I and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The trial court's judgment was affirmed on appeal. First, the court found that appellant had failed to direct the court's attention to any specific statutory language alleged to be indefinite, vague, or uncertain. Because § 43.21 had previously been held to be constitutional, the court declined to engage in a search for unconstitutionality. Moreover, the trial court was found to have properly denied appellant's motion to quash. The court found that § 43.21 passed constitutional muster because it did not inject considerations of community standards into separate determination of the work's value.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below, which convicted appellant of selling obscene material, was affirmed on appeal. The court declined engage in a search for unconstitutionality in the Texas Obscenity Statute, which had previously been held to be constitutional, because appellant failed to direct the court's attention to any alleged indefinite, vague, or uncertain language.

 

875 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Drummond v. State


No. 01-87-00767-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


752 S.W.2d 181; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1262



June 2, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 950,142.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 4, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of selling obscene materials as defined in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1) (1988). Appellant argues that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motion to quash, asserting that § 43.21(a)(1) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In his motion to quash, appellant failed to point out exactly what part of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1) (1988) was unconstitutionally vague. Thus he preserved nothing for review. Even in his brief, appellant did not identify which portion of the law was vague, and did not identify a risk or detriment to which he had been exposed without fair warning. Thus he presented nothing for review. To the extent the issue had been litigated in other cases, the statute had been upheld, and the court affirmed the denial of the motion to quash as to appellant's vagueness claim. Appellant also claimed that § 43.21(a)(1) was not in line with recent United States Supreme Court jurisprudence, and that the trial court had not made a determination that the materials he sold were obscene. As to the latter point, the court noted that appellant had pleaded no contest, had not raised this argument in his motion, and had not obtained the trial court's permission to argue it on appeal. The Helms rule survived in appellant's circumstance. The court then held that the "contemporary community standards" language of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1)(A) (1988) had not been repudiated or superceded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for selling obscene material. The court held that appellant had not properly preserved or presented his void for vagueness claim as to the obscenity law. Having pleaded no contest without benefit of a plea bargain, he could not complain of an unpreserved nonjurisdictional defect. Texas obscenity law comported with current constitutional jurisprudence.

Mendoza v. State


No. 01-86-00457-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1263



June 2, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 268th District Court, Fort Bend County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 16,060


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of his conviction of burglary of a habitation from the 268th District Court, Fort Bend County, (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner challenged his conviction of burglary because his right to a speedy trial had been denied. The court noted that U.S. Const. amend VI and Tex. Const. art. I § 10 guaranteed the right to a speedy trial. The court stated that appellant made no showing of prejudice as required under the speedy trial analysis and the court held that the six-month delay did not deprive appellant of his constitutional right to a speedy trial. The court held that appellant failed to preserve his challenges to the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress his statement and appellee state's introduction of photographs of the crime scene. Appellant's objections at trial did not comport with his points of error on appeal therefore nothing was preserved for review pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 52(a). Appellant also waived his allegation of misuse of peremptory challenges because he failed to provide a transcript of voir dire. Affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant prisoner's conviction of burglary of a habitation was affirmed. A six month delay from the time of indictment to trial was not a violation of appellant's speedy trial rights because appellant failed to make a showing of prejudice due to the delay.

Pittman v. State


No. 01-87-00717-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1268



June 2, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 950,715


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere to a charge of selling obscene materials in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County (Texas), and was sentenced to three days confinement in the county jail and a fine. On appeal, the appellant contended error in the denial of is pretrial motion to quash on the basis that Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43.21(a) (1988) of the Texas Obscenity Statute violated the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere to a charge of selling obscene materials, and received a three-day sentence in the county jail and a fine. Appellant challenged the trial court conviction against him contending error in the denial of his pretrial motion to quash on the basis that Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43.21(a) (1988) of the Texas Obscenity Statute violated U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. The court examined the statute and looked at precedent pertaining to the state obscenity laws, which held that its unconstitutionality had to be attacked with regard to specific applications. Appellant did not state any unconstitutional application in his challenge, thus, the presumption of the statute's constitutionality was unrebutted. Appellant also contended that sufficient evidence did not support his conviction under the obscenity statute. The court stated that, since appellant had not raised the matter below in his nolo contendere plea, he was unable to argue that point on appeal. Concluding that the Texas Obscenity Statute complied with United States Supreme Court precedent for such laws and was valid, the trial court judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment convicting appellant on his nolo contendere plea to selling obscene materials. The court concluded that appellant had not enumerated any examples of an unconstitutional application as it related to the obscenity law, thus the presumption of the statute's constitutionality remained intact.

882 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Long v. State


No. 01-87-00196-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1279



June 2, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 466,439


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), where he had been convicted for aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child. He contended that his counsel had been ineffective because he failed to challenge one of the jurors for cause, object to the jury instruction on the parole law, object and preserve error to the prosecutor's closing argument at guilt/innocence, and object to the prosecutor's closing argument at punishment. The court affirmed. Without ruling whether the juror should have been struck for cause, the court held that appellant failed to show that one or more objectionable jurors sat on the jury, as was required. Five courts had upheld the constitutionality of the parole charge, including this court. Even if it was error for counsel to fail to object, the error did not warrant automatic dismissal. After considering the totality of the evidence, the grievous nature of the crime, and the fact that appellant received only a 20-year sentence, the court held that the trial court's inclusion of the parole charge was harmless. Comments responding to opposing counsel's argument were appropriate. Any other error in the state's closing argument was harmless. A prosecutor may argue his opinion as long as it is based on the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child, because his contentions of ineffective assistance of counsel at trial were without merit. Even though counsel could have struck a juror for cause, appellant failed to show that one or more objectionable jurors had sat on the jury. Constitutionality of the parole charge given, and complained of by appellant, had been upheld by five courts, including this court.

Grantham v. State


No. 2-86-093-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


751 S.W.2d 321; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1500



June 2, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 28, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 1 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Criminal District Court No. 1, Tarrant County (Texas), where he had been convicted for attempted capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of attempted capital murder. He contended that the trial court erred by instructing the jurors on parole eligibility where the charge was inconsistent and confusing; the charge was not authorized since Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. § 37.07(4)(a) only authorized the charge in connection with offenses listed in Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. § 42.12, and § 42.12 has no subsection (3f)(a)(1) or (3f)(a)(2); the giving of the charge violated the doctrine of the separation of power between the executive and judicial branch, as required by Tex. Const. art I, § 1. The court affirmed. Appellant made only a general objection to the trial court's instruction, which failed to preserve error. The instruction was improperly given because it constituted an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers, but he suffered no egregious harm. The court had previously held that the charge at issue was not unconstitutionally vague. Regarding subsection (3f)(a)(1) or (3f)(a)(2) in § 42.12, the legislature clearly intended the reference to be to section 3g(a)(1) and 3g(a) (2) and that such a clerical error was to be disregarded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court convicting appellant of capital murder because he only made a general objection to the jury instruction in question, which failed to preserve error. He failed to show that the error was fundamental and that he had suffered egregious harm.

Hernandez v. State


No. 690-86


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


751 S.W.2d 513; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1231



June 1, 1988, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Thirteenth Court of Appeals, Corpus Christi (Texas), rejecting the state's contention that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. II, § 32A.02 violated the separation of powers provision of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1 and that its caption violated Tex. Const. art III, § 35.


OVERVIEW: The state sought review of the lower court's judgment holding that Tex. Code Crim P. Ann. art. 32A.02 was constitutionally valid. The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded for review of appellant's other points of error that had not yet been reviewed by the lower court. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32A.02 was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers provision of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. In a decision of the court, handed down after the lower court decided the action, the court declared art. 32A.02 unconstitutional and void in its entirety because the legislature in enacting the statute violated the separation of powers provision of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. The court, however, held that art. 32A.02 was not unconstitutional based on its caption because Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 provided that an act of the legislature could not be declared unconstitutional due to a deficiency of the statute's caption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held that the statute was unconstitutional because the legislature in enacting the statute violated the separation of powers provision of the state constitution. The court, however, held that the statute was not unconstitutional based on its caption because no act of the legislature could be declared unconstitutional due to a deficiency of the statute's caption.

El Paso v. El Paso Jaycees

886 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Schrader v. State


No. 3-87-034-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


753 S.W.2d 733; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1953



June 1, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF TRAVIS COUNTY NO. 271-731, HONORABLE LESLIE D. TAYLOR, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Court at Law No. 1 of Travis County (Texas) which found him guilty of resisting arrest pursuant to Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 38.03 (1974).


OVERVIEW: Officers detained appellant in a restaurant parking lot after he was ejected for creating a drunken disturbance. Upon learning that there was an outstanding warrant for appellant, one of the officer's advised him that he was under arrest. When the officers attempted to handcuff appellant, he resisted by kicking, hitting, and biting one of the officers. The trial court found appellant guilty under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.03 (1974) of resisting arrest. On appeal, appellant contended that he was already under arrest at the time he assaulted the officer and thus could not be convicted under § 38.03. Affirming the conviction, the court found that the officers were "effecting an arrest" within the meaning of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.03(a) (1974) when they attempted to handcuff appellant under authority of the newly discovered arrest warrant. While appellant's arrest was complete with his detention in the parking lot five minutes earlier for some purposes of the law, the court found, other purposes did not preclude the officers' handcuffing him to reduce him to actual or physical restraint, pursuant to the definition of "arrest" under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 15.22 (1977).


OUTCOME: Finding the evidence sufficient to support a finding that appellant could be convicted of resisting arrest, even though he had been detained five minutes earlier, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Amescua v. State


Appeal No. 04-85-00482-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


751 S.W.2d 709; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1451



May 31, 1988, Decided  
May 31, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 25th District Court of Guadalupe County, Trial Court No. 85-53, Honorable B.B. Schraub, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant's petition for discretionary review of a conviction of indecency with a child was granted by the Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas); the case was remanded for reconsideration of appellant's points of error relating to the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (1988). Appellant claimed that as a result of the videotaped testimony of the child-complainant, appellant was denied the right to confront the witness.


OVERVIEW: An appeal from a conviction of indecency with a child was remanded for reconsideration of appellant's points of error relating to the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (1988). On remand, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. Based on a decision of the court of criminal appeals handed down after the court's affirmation of the trial court's judgment, the court held that art. 38.071, § 2 was unconstitutional because it deprived appellant of his right of confrontation and due process and due course of law on both federal and state grounds. Appellant was denied the opportunity to cross-examine the child-complainant contemporaneously with the making of the videotape of the child's testimony. Additionally, appellant had to call the child to testify in order to cross-examine her, thereby running the risk of incurring the wrath of the jury and inflaming the jury to the extent of making the trial fundamentally unfair. Because the court could not conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that the error made no contribution to the conviction, Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2) mandated reversal and a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial based on a recent decision of the court of criminal appeals. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional because it deprived appellant of his right of confrontation and due process on both federal and state grounds. Appellant was denied the opportunity to cross-examine the child-complainant contemporaneously with the videotaped testimony of the child.

 

888 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Med-Safe, Inc. v. State


No. 01-88-0047-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


752 S.W.2d 638; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1152



May 26, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 165th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 87-23,401, DAVID WEST, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged the issuance of a temporary injunction by the 165th District Court, Harris County (Texas) that prohibited the operation of appellants' non-hazardous solid waste site until a permit was issued by appellee, the Texas Department of Health. Appellants contended error in the issuance of the temporary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The state obtained a temporary injunction in the trial court against appellant company that prohibited the operation of appellants' non-hazardous solid waste site until a permit was issued by the state through appellee, its department of health. Appellant company challenged the issuance of a temporary injunction contending error because the Solid Waste Disposal Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4477-7, §§ 3(a), 4(e) (Supp. 1988), and other state health department regulations, were not constitutional delegations of legislative authority. Appellant contended that these laws precluded the delegation of legislative authority, including allowing appellee state health department to license solid waste disposal sites. The court noted that the legislature had authority to delegate to an administrative agency the authority to establish minimum standards that reasonably carried out the expressed purpose of a statutory act. The court determined that the Act provided adequate guidelines to the state to establish rules and regulations to reasonably carry out the express purposes of the Act, including the licensing of solid waste disposal sites. The trial court judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the issuance of the temporary injunction against appellant company. The court concluded that the Solid Waste Disposal Act (Act) and other state health department regulations were not unconstitutional delegations of legislative authority, but rather established rules and regulations that reasonably carried out the Act's purposes including allowing the state health department to license solid waste disposal sites.

Singleton v. State


No. A14-87-00403-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 316; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1167



May 26, 1988, Decided  
May 26, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 463,305.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 209th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of burglarizing a habitation. Appellant argued that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4) was unconstitutional on separation of powers and due course of law grounds under the Texas Constitution. Appellant also argued that the prosecutor's peremptory strikes violated the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglarizing a habitation. Upon appellant's plea of true to an enhancement paragraph in the indictment, the jury assessed his punishment at 30 years. The trial court's jury charge included a parole charge pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4). Appellant first point of error on appeal argued that art. 37.07(4) was unconstitutional on separation of powers and due course of law grounds under the Texas Constitution. The court overruled appellant's first point of error because the instruction was not shown to have caused harm. Appellant's second point of error claimed that the prosecutor's peremptory strikes violated the Equal Protection Clause. The court overruled appellant's second point of error because appellant failed to carry his ultimate burden of proving that the prosecutor's neutral explanations for dismissing black members from the jury venire were a mere pretext for discrimination. Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for burglarizing a habitation was affirmed. Appellant's constitutionality argument concerning the jury parole charge was overruled because the instruction caused no harm. The court overruled appellant's claim that the prosecutor's use of peremptory challenges violated the Equal Protection Clause because appellant failed to prove that the prosecutor's neutral explanations were a mere pretext for discrimination.

Allen v. State


No. 01-87-00461-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 931; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1174



May 26, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 464,216, A.D. Azios, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 57 years in prison and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction of aggravated robbery, appellant sought review and contended that the trial court erred in denying his request for a Batson hearing and his motion to strike the jury panel. Appellant alleged that, through its use of peremptory strikes, the state engaged in the systematic exclusion of members of appellant's racial group from the jury. The court found that appellant had established a prima facie showing of purposeful discrimination because he was black, the prosecutor struck black jurors, and the prosecutor's use of her peremptory strikes caused four of only six possible black jurors to be struck. The court held that the burden was therefore on the state to produce neutral explanations for its challenges to those jurors who shared appellant's race. After reviewing the reasons given by the prosecutor, the court held that she effectively rebutted the presumption of race discrimination. Appellant also objected to the trial court's use of an instruction pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) because the statute had been held to be unconstitutional. The court determined that the error was harmless and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of aggravated robbery because it found that the prosecution had effectively rebutted a presumption of purposeful discrimination in the selection of the jury by providing race-neutral reasons for the use of its peremptory strikes.

 

891 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Crabb v. State


Nos. 01-87-00379-CR, 01-87-00380-CR, 01-87-00381-CR, 01-87-00382-CR, 01-87-00383-CR, 01-87-00384-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


754 S.W.2d 742; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1175



May 26, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended May 27, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 912,852, 912,858, 912,859, 912,860, 912,865, 912,867, Hannah Chow, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of judgments from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5 of Harris County, Texas, that convicted them of criminal trespass for their occupation of an abortion clinic. Appellants claimed they were deprived of due process when the trial court excluded evidence of necessity, defense of others, and justification, and that the conditions of probation violated their free speech rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellants' proffered evidence concerning harm to the unborn was inadmissible and properly excluded, as evidence concerning when life begins, development characteristics of the unborn child, and the effects of an abortion upon an unborn child were irrelevant to the crime of criminal trespass. Exclusion of other testimony concerning appellants' motivation was proper, because appellants had failed to raise a fact issue concerning necessity, defense of others, or justification. The harm sought to be avoided, namely abortions, was not greater than the harm from the abrogation of patients' privacy rights. This negated an essential element of the statutory necessity defense, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 9.22 (1974). Defense of third persons was likewise unavailable, as a fetus was not a person under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 1.07(a)(17), (27). Similarly, nobody's life or health was being threatened at the clinic, so Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 9.34(b) (1974) was inapplicable. The probation order enjoined appellants from demonstrating or picketing the clinic. This imposition on appellants' free speech right was not unconstitutional, as it was directly related to their transgressions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' criminal trespass convictions. The court found no abuse of discretion in the exclusion of irrelevant evidence relating to defenses not germane to the facts. The restrictions imposed as conditions of probation were appropriate to the offenses and not unconstitutional.
