Herring v. State


No. 01-87-00736-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


752 S.W.2d 169; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1195



May 26, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 479273.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of aggravated assault, found an enhancement allegation to be true, and assessed punishment at 10 years confinement and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction for aggravated assault, appellant sought review of the judgment and contended that the trial court committed reversible error in refusing to grant a severance of the offenses alleged in the indictment. The court held that if any error occurred, it was harmless because evidence of the burglary was admissible to show the context in which the aggravated assault occurred. Appellant next asserted that the trial court erred in permitting testimony about an extraneous offense that occurred on the night of the crime because the prosecution failed to give notice of their intent to use the extraneous offense. The court noted that Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 404(b) required notice only of those extraneous offenses that were to be introduced in the state's case-in-chief. The court held that because the offense of which appellant complained was not admitted until after the defense rested, no violation of the rule took place. After considering and rejecting appellant's remaining allegations of trial court error, the court reformed the judgment to include an affirmative finding of a deadly weapon and affirmed the judgment as reformed.


OUTCOME: The court reformed the judgment to include an affirmative finding of a deadly weapon. The court affirmed the judgment as reformed because it found appellant failed to establish that any reversible error occurred during the trial.

Tucker v. State


No. 2-87-041-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


751 S.W.2d 919; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1945



May 25, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. THREE OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Criminal District Court, No. Three of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted appellant of solicitation of capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 15.03 (1974) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03 (Supp. 1988), and found true a sentence enhancement for a prior felony conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of solicitation of capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 15.03 (1974) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03 (Supp. 1988). The jury found true a sentence enhancement for a prior felony conviction in another state. Appellant alleged that he was denied a speedy trial, that the indictment was defective, and that there was error in denying his requested jury charge on specific intent. The court affirmed, holding that the 18-month delay between arrest and trial was not violative of the speedy trial rights. The indictment properly contained the statutory words as to specific conduct and circumstances of the offense. There was no error in denying appellant's motion for an instructed verdict based upon insufficient evidence of venue because there was sufficient evidence that the offense was committed in the county where the trial was held. The state's motion for rehearing was granted because the court held that its reversal of the sentence enhancement on appellant's prior appeal was in error because, although the evidence of judgment of the prior conviction failed to meet the requirement for a judgment in Texas, there was sufficient evidence of the prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order convicting appellant of solicitation of capital murder because the indictment of the offense was proper, appellant was not denied his right to a speedy trial, and there was sufficient evidence supporting venue.

 

894 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lapasnick v. State


Appeal No. 04-87-00179-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


751 S.W.2d 880; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1932



May 24, 1988, Decided  
May 24, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 751 S.W.2d 880 at 882. Petition for Discretionary Denied February 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of March 31, 1988, Reported at: 751 S.W.2d 880. Appeal from County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 383,906, Honorable Timothy Johnson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND THE CAUSE IS ORDERED DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal challenged the order of the County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County (Texas) that denied him habeas corpus relief. Appellant asserted that a second prosecution for driving while intoxicated was barred as a prior complaint and information that charged the identical offense had been dismissed by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The state's case against appellant criminal for driving while intoxicated was dismissed by the trial court because the state failed to comply with the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1988). The state filed a second complaint and information charging the same offense, alleging that appellant could not rely on the Speedy Trial Act and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 because they were declared unconstitutional. The court held that the subsequent declaration of the unconstitutionality of the Speedy Trial Act had no effect on the finality of the judgment. The law in effect at the time that appellant's cause was dismissed, art. 28.061, constituted a bar to further prosecution for the same offense because it provided that a discharge for failure to provide a speedy trial barred any other further prosecution for any offense arising out of the same transaction. Thus, the court held that once the trial court signed the judgment of dismissal, the judgment became final, and the jurisdiction of the same court over the same cause was exhausted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that denied appellant criminal habeas corpus relief because the judgment of dismissal had become final and the trial court lacked jurisdiction to try appellant a second time for the exact same offense of driving while intoxicated.

 

895 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cedar Crest #10, Inc. v. Dallas


No. 11-87-112-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1090



May 19, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn June 16, 1988; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2043.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 162nd District Court of Dallas County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant building owner sought review of the judgment of the 162nd District Court of Dallas County, Texas, in favor of appellee city, that allowed city to demolish appellant's apartment building as a public nuisance under Dallas, Tex. Rev. City Code ch. 27 (1960), on the grounds that the statute deprived appellant of his right to due process of law, appellee's action was barred by estoppel, and that there was no trial on the merits.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of appellee city, which affirmed a nuisance finding against appellant building owner's building. The court held that Dallas, Tex. Rev. City Code ch. 27 (1960) was constitutional under U.S. Const. amend. V or Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. The court found that ch. 27 provided for notices of violation, hearing date, and order of demolition, as well as judicial review. Appellee availed himself of these procedural safeguards, which afforded appellant due process. The court found that the substantial evidence rule provided by ch. 27 did not prevent a judicial determination of the alleged nuisance. The court held that recitations and presumptions contained in the judgment proved a trial. The court held that appellee was not judicially estopped by an opinion that held appellant's building was not a nuisance. The court found that in that action, appellee asserted appellant's building was a nuisance under Dallas, Tex. Rev. City Code ch. 16, which did not estop appellee from asserting that the building was a nuisance under ch. 27.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment that affirmed board finding of nuisance against appellee building owner's building was affirmed because city code provided for a judicial determination of the fact of nuisance, the judgment reflected the trial court held a hearing on the merits, and estoppel did not apply because appellee city could seek nuisance determination under different code chapters.

Smith v. State


No. B14-87-281-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 902; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1115



May 19, 1988, Decided  
May 19, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended July 19, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from [TEXT DELETED BY COURT EMENDATION] 176th District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 86,213.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought post-conviction review of robbery by assault conviction under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. arts. 36.28 and 36.31, in favor of appellee state in the 176th District Court of Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought post-conviction relief from his robbery by assault conviction in favor of appellee state based on the contention he was denied a complete statement of facts and transcript for appeal and the right to effective assistance of counsel. The court rejected the argument that the alleged failure to include a note sent by the jury rendered the record incomplete when there was nothing to show appellant was precluded from excepting to the action of the trial court. The court noted the lower court held a hearing on appellant's claim and determined he did not establish the existence of any note by the judge in response to jury inquiry. The court next rejected appellant's claim of ineffective assistance. The court explained appellant failed to establish deficient performance by his attorney when counsel's performance was reasonable under prevailing professional norms. The court elaborated by noting that without a showing of harm, the failure to request recordation of voir dire or closing argument was not per se ineffectiveness and that an isolated failure to object to certain procedural mistakes did not demonstrate ineffectiveness either.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's robbery by assault conviction in favor of appellee state because appellant was not denied a complete record on appeal when no showing of an alleged note by the trial judge in response to a jury note was shown, and appellant failed to establish requisite deficient performance by counsel when his attorney rendered reasonable professional assistance under prevailing norms.

Haughton v. State


No. A14-87-00265-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 899; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1040



May 12, 1988, Decided  
May 12, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied March 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 454,555.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant sought review of his conviction in the 338th District Court of Harris County (Texas), for aggravated sexual assault of a minor. Appellant contended that the trial court erred when it admitted a videotaped statement, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the conviction, that the prosecutor made improper jury arguments, and that the prosecution improperly recalled the complainant after other witnesses had testified.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for the aggravated sexual assault of his 10-year-old niece. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence enhancement. The court held that, although Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 38.071, § 2 had been declared unconstitutional, the complainant's videotaped accusation was admissible under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 801(e)(1)(B) and Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 402. The court held that even though the prosecution referred to the complainant's vagina areas and not the complainant's vagina, a rational jury could have found contact between appellant's penis and the complainant's vagina beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the prosecutor did not comment upon appellant's failure to testify because a comment about rehabilitation could have been directed towards the testimony of other witnesses. The record did not indicate that the prosecution referred to parole instead of sentencing. The court held that the trial court properly allowed the prosecution to recall the complainant to explain that she recanted her videotaped accusation when she first testified because she was scared of appellant.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed. The videotaped statement of the complainant was properly admitted, the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict, the prosecution's comments were not improper, and the complainant was properly recalled to testify.

Gray v. State


No. A14-87-00370-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1049



May 12, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 463,199


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 178th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery. Appellant alleged that the trial court erred in its instructions to the jury, that the prosecution improperly challenged jurors, and that the trial court erred in its admission of evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery and alleged that the trial court erred in its instructions to the jury, that jurors were improperly subjected to peremptory challenges, that the prosecution gave an improper closing argument, and that the trial court erred when it admitted certain evidence. The court affirmed, finding that appellant suffered no harm from the instructions given to the jury. While procedure prescribed by Batson v. Kentucky, 476 U.S. 79, 106 S.Ct. 1712, 90 L.Ed.2d 69 (1986), had to be followed, appellant also had to make a timely objection to the prosecution's use of peremptory challenges. Appellant failed to do so; therefore, no complaint regarding the prosecution's peremptory challenges was preserved for review. With regard to appellant's other challenges, the record was facially defective in almost all regards, through waiver and lack of timely objections, and no errors had been preserved for the court's review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery was upheld, because the charge given to the jury resulted in no harm to appellant, appellant's complaints regarding jury challenges and the improper admission of certain evidence were not properly preserved for appeal.

Elizondo v. Ft. Bend Independent School Dist.


No. 01-87-00926-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1066



May 12, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 268th District Court, Fort Bend County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 58,418


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of an order of the 268th District Court, Fort Bend County (Texas), which denied appellants' request for a temporary injunction that would have allowed appellants' minor child to attend school in appellee school district.


OVERVIEW: Appellant parents' minor child lived apart from his parents and in appellee school district. Appellee refused to enroll the minor child in its schools, because appellee's policy required that students reside in the district with parents, legal guardians, or other persons with lawful control over the child. Appellants filed suit alleging that appellee's policy violated the state and federal constitutions and was contrary to the Texas Education Code. They requested a temporary restraining order to restore the status quo. The trial court denied appellants' request, and appellants filed an interlocutory appeal. The court affirmed, finding that the trial court's action was not so arbitrary as to exceed the bounds of reasonable discretion when it denied the appellants' request for a temporary injunction. Appellants, when they sought to enjoin appellee, actually sought to alter the status quo, because the minor child was already enrolled in another school district. Furthermore, appellants failed to show a probable right of recovery at trial.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. Appellant parents were properly denied temporary injunctive relief to permit their child to attend school in a particular school district, because the trial court's action was not so arbitrary as to exceed the bounds of reasonable discretion when it denied the appellants' request for a temporary injunction. Appellants sought to alter the status quo and failed to show a probable right of recovery at trial.

Hellman v. Mateo


No. 01-87-00340-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 623; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1073



May 12, 1988, Decided  
May 12, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Motion for Rehearing Denied June 16, 1988, Reported at: 751 S.W.2d 623 at 628.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 281st District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 85-49616.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged an order of the 281st District Court, Harris County (Texas), granting summary judgment to appellees, a pathologist and a hospital, in appellant's medical malpractice action, which alleged that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590I, § 10.01 (1987), a statute of absolute limitation violated the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, former patient, brought a medical malpractice action against appellees, a pathologist and a hospital, for appellee pathologist's misdiagnosis of a biopsy. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of a summary judgment to appellees, holding that appellant's action was barred by the absolute two-year limitation for such actions, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590I, § 10.01 (1987). Appellant argued that the statute violated the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 3. The court held that the statute's constitutionality was upheld unless a plaintiff affirmatively showed that her cause of action was not barred before she could reasonably have discovered the wrong and filed suit. Appellant had burden of proof on the issue, not appellees, but she did not address the issue in her answer or her response to summary judgment; thus she could not prevail on appeal. The court rejected appellant's argument that the statute should have been tolled because she raised a fact issue about her lack of knowledge that a wrong occurred because the issue was whether she reasonably could have discovered the wrong in two years, not whether she in fact did.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. Appellees, a pathologist and a hospital, were entitled to summary judgment in appellant former patient's medical malpractice action, which was precluded by the statute of limitations. The absolute statute of limitations that barred her claim did not violate the state constitution, because it allowed such actions if a plaintiff could not have discovered the alleged wrong within the two year time period.

 

901 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Vinson v. Burgess


No. 2-87-069-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


755 S.W.2d 481; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 2268



May 12, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 755 S.W.2d 481 at 483. Opinion on Rehearing August 18, 1988, Reported at: 755 S.W.2d 481 at 484.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original opinion of January 14, 1988, Reported at: 755 S.W.2d 481. APPEAL FROM THE 211TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees filed a motion for rehearing of an order that reversed an order of the 211th District Court, Denton County (Texas), that did not uphold Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 26.07 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued an order that did not uphold Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 26.07 (1988), which authorized an election to roll back tax rates set by a commissioner's court, regardless of the constitutionality of the rate set. The court reversed the trial court's order, and appellees filed a motion for rehearing. The court granted the motion for rehearing and found that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to counties because the statute conflicted directly with Tex. Const. art. VIII, §§ 1-a and 9, which authorized commissioners' courts of each county to set the tax rate subject only to the ceilings stated in the constitution. As the statute was unconstitutional and the court could not compel a compliance with an unconstitutional statute, the court set aside its initial decision reversing the trial court, and affirmed the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: Appellees' motion for rehearing was granted, and the court reversed its initial order and affirmed the trial court's order because the statute at issue was unconstitutional and unenforceable.

 

902 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Worrell v. State


No. 01-87-00524-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 566; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 940



May 5, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 419,143.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for second degree felony possession of marijuana and sentence of two years' incarceration, entered in the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), pursuant to a plea bargain.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pled guilty in the trial court to the second degree felony of possession of marijuana and received a sentence of two years' incarceration, pursuant to a plea bargain, he appealed. Defendant contended his plea was rendered involuntary because a higher court foreclosed his right to appeal the merits of his Speedy Trial Act claim by adjudicating that act unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court judgment, agreeing with the state's contention on appeal that defendant equated the right to a forum and an opportunity to present his claim with the substantive right to a favorable ruling on the claim. The court reasoned that defendant was not procedurally prevented from asserting his claim, even though it was moot. Additionally, the change in the substantive law did not render defendant's trial court plea involuntary, and the change in the substantive law occurred prior to defendant's plea, thereby precluding detrimental reliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that a higher court's decision as to the unconstitutionality of the speedy trial statute, which rendered defendant's speedy trial claim moot, did not foreclose his procedural right to appeal the speedy trial claim or render his trial court guilty plea involuntary.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the County Court at Law Number Twelve, Harris County (Texas) sentence of three days' incarceration and a $ 350 fine, imposed pursuant to defendant's plea of nolo contendere to the misdemeanor offense of selling obscene material.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled nolo contendere to the misdemeanor offense of selling obscene material and sustained a trial court sentence of three days' incarceration and a fine of $ 350. 904 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lopez v. State


No. 01-87-00307-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 949



May 5, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 435,964


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with murder, pleaded not guilty, and was convicted of involuntary manslaughter. Complainant died after being shot in the back and witnesses testified that appellant shot complainant from a few feet away. Appellant maintained that someone took his pistol and that he heard the gunfire when complainant was behind him. On appeal, appellant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because it was not consistent with the nature of the wounds inflicted upon the complainant and there was no evidence that he acted recklessly. The court rejected this argument and held that there was sufficient evidence to find that appellant shot complainant from a few feet and that appellant was reckless due to his use of a deadly weapon. The court also rejected appellant's claim that the trial court erred when it denied his motion for dismissal for failure to afford appellant his constitutional statutory rights to a speedy trial in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI, Tex. Const. art. I § 10, and Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. art. 1.03, 1.04, 1.05 (1977). The court noted that appellant waived his right to a speedy trial. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support his conviction because the evidence was consistent with complainant's wounds and appellant's use of a gun provided evidence that he acted recklessly. The court found that the trial court did not violate appellant's constitutional rights to a speedy trial when it denied appellant's motion for dismissal.

 

905 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Kowey v. State


No. C14-87-00267-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 587; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1229



May 5, 1988, Decided  
May 5, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion of March 31, 1988 Withdrawn


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 431,734


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 337th District Court Harris County (Texas), entering his conviction for aggravated sexual assault and sentencing him to life imprisonment after the jury found him guilty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault, the jury having found defendant's acts or words placed the victim in fear that death, serious bodily injury or kidnapping would be imminently inflicted on her, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(2) (1987). On appeal, the court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment based on the state's failure to comply with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1987), because that statute was unconstitutional. Defendant was not denied a speedy trial, because the state did not deliberately attempt to delay the trial in order to hamper defendant's defense and the trial delay was occasioned in substantial part by his incarceration and his trials associated with prior offenses. Testimony regarding the two extraneous offenses committed by appellant showed a similarity between the two previous rape offenses and this offense, and thus was admissible on the issue of identity. The evidence was sufficient to prove that complainant was in fear that death would be imminently inflicted on her. Accordingly, the court affirmed the holding of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that entered his conviction for aggravated sexual assault. The court held that defendant was not denied a speedy trial, because the trial was delayed because of his incarceration and his trials associated with prior offenses.

 

906 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Texas Dep't of Public Safety v. Sefcik


Appeal No. 04-87-00687-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


751 S.W.2d 239; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1487



April 29, 1988, Decided  
April 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the County Probate Court No. 2 of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 173152, Honorable Keith Burris, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas Department of Public Safety (DPS) challenged the decision of the Probate Court No. 2 of Bexar County (Texas), which probated the suspension of appellee driver's license for refusal to take a breath test or offer a blood sample. Appellant claimed that an amendment to Tex. Civ. Stat. Ann art. 6687(b), § 22 (e) (1987) withdrew the trial court's discretion to grant probation in breath test refusal cases.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Texas Department of Public Safety (DPS) sought review of the trial court's grant of probation of the suspension of the driver's license of appellee driver for his refusal to take a breath test following his arrest for driving under the influence. Appellant argued that the amendment to Tex. Civ. Stat. Ann art. 6687(b), § 22 (e) (1987), which took effect after appellee's arrest but prior to his trial, withdrew the trial court's discretion to grant probation in breath test refusal cases. The court disagreed, finding that under the Texas Code Construction Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 311.031(a)(3) and (4) (1988), the law in effect at the time of the violation governed the punishment. Thus, the trial court had discretion based upon the law in existence at the time of the offense to probate the suspension of appellee's driver's license. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment probating appellee driver's license suspension for refusing to take breath test after being arrested for driving under the influence. Although the statute had been amended withdrawing the trial court's discretion to award probation, appellee's sentence was governed by the law in effect at the time of the refusal to take the test.

 

907 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lindsay v. Papageorgiou


No. 01-86-00941-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


751 S.W.2d 544; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 922



April 28, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 295th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-35067.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county judge sought review of the order of the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which entered a declaratory judgment declaring unconstitutional §§ 6(a) and 6(b) of the Regulations of Harris County, Texas for the location of certain sexually oriented commercial enterprises and permanently enjoined appellants from enforcing the regulations, and awarded attorney fees to appellee, the nude dance club owner and operator.


OVERVIEW: Appellee owned and operated an establishment that provided topless entertainment. Appellee was arrested for operating a sexually oriented commercial enterprise in the county and outside the corporate limits of a city, without a permit. Appellee then applied for a permit and was denied because her establishment was located within 1500 feet of a residential neighborhood, in violation of a local regulation. Appellee filed a cause of action and sought a declaratory judgment that the county regulations were unconstitutional and requested injunctive relief prohibiting appellant county judge from enforcing them in the future. The lower court declared unconstitutional §§ 6(a) and 6(b) of the Regulations of Harris County, Texas for the location of certain sexually oriented commercial enterprises and permanently enjoined appellants from enforcing the regulations. The court reversed the lower court's judgment because the county regulations were constitutional. The regulations imposed only a minimal or incidental burden on protected expression; they were nothing more than a limitation on the place where such expression was exercised. Thus, appellee's U.S. Const. amend. I challenge was met.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order, which entered a declaratory judgment declaring unconstitutional certain county regulations location of certain sexually oriented commercial enterprises, permanently enjoined appellants from enforcing the regulations, and awarded appellee nude dance club owner attorneys' fees because the regulations restricting appellee's business in proximity to other establishments and residences was constitutional.

Donaldson v. State


No. 01-87-00492-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 971



April 28, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 469,140


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault of a child and assessed a punishment of 20 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant enticed minor complainant, a child, and her aunt to his apartment where he threatened them with a gun unless they cooperated with him in sexual conduct. Defendant sexually abused the child over a 12-hour period until the aunt escaped and summoned the police. The state notified defendant eight days prior to trial that it intended to call the child's grandmother to testify about an oral outcry made after the attack. During the trial the aunt testified that a co-defendant purchased cocaine from defendant during the attack. The gun used by defendant was also admitted into evidence. Defendant was found guilty of aggravated sexual assault of a child and claimed on appeal that the trial court erroneously admitted into evidence the gun, evidence of other crimes, and hearsay; that the state did not provide timely notice of intent to introduce complainant's outcry; and that the jury charge on the law of parole was unconstitutional. The court rejected defendant's contention and affirmed the conviction. The court found that the trial court did not err in admitting the evidence in question, and that any error was harmless in light of the evidence against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault of a child. The court found that the defendant was not harmed by introduction of the complainant's outcry made after the attack, by introduction of the gun used to threaten complainant, or by testimony that defendant was using and selling cocaine during the attack.

Brown v. State


No. 09-87-209 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


750 S.W.2d 340; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1373



April 28, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment by the Criminal District Court of Jefferson County (Texas), which convicted him of burglary of a habitation. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to allow defense counsel to cross-examine the prosecution as to why a prospective juror was dismissed, in denying a request for a mistrial based on an improper prosecution argument, and in submitting an instruction regarding parole law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary of a habitation. On appeal, he contended that the trial court erred in refusing to allow defense counsel to cross-examine the prosecution as to why a prospective juror was dismissed, in denying a request for a mistrial based on improper prosecution arguments, and in submitting an instruction regarding parole law. The court rejected these contentions and affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that appellant waived any error by the trial court in refusing to allow cross-examination of the prosecution as to the use of a peremptory challenge because appellant failed to make an offer of proof as to the excluded testimony. The court found that the prosecution's improper jury arguments did not constitute reversible error because the trial court's instruction to the jury to disregard the argument was sufficient to cure the harmful effect. Appellant did not properly preserve any error for review as to the propriety of giving the statutory parole law instruction because appellant's brief on appeal did not comport with his objections at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of burglary of a habitation. The court found that appellant waived error by the trial court in refusing to allow cross-examination of the prosecutor as to the use of a peremptory challenge. The trial court's instruction to the jury was sufficient to cure the harmful effect of prosecution's improper jury arguments. Appellant waived error as to the statutory parole law instruction.

Madrid v. State


No. 08-87-00290-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


751 S.W.2d 226; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 903



April 27, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 120th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC No. 50682).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered by the El Paso County Criminal Law Magistrate, presiding for the judge of the 120th Judicial District Court (Texas), which convicted defendant for burglary of a vehicle founded upon a plea of guilty.


OVERVIEW: A judgment was entered by the El Paso County Criminal Law Magistrate upon defendant's plea of guilty to the offense of burglary of a vehicle. Defendant raised six points of error on appeal, which challenged the constitutionality of the El Paso Criminal Law Magistrate's Court, created by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 1918g (1988). The court rejected each constitutional claim presented by defendant and affirmed the conviction. The court ruled that article 1918g was a constitutional legislative method which provided for an increase in the caseload of the criminal courts, and that the magistrate had county-wide authority even though the town of Vinton was excluded from its jurisdiction. The court found that the magistrate's court did not violate the election requirements of Tex. Const. Art. V, § 7 because the magistrates were appointed by the district court and did not have coextensive powers. The court also found that defendant was not deprived of her right to appeal because all appealable decisions from the magistrate were issued in his capacity as presiding the referring district judge and not from the magistrate's court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the a judgement from the El Paso County Criminal Law Magistrate which convicted defendant for burglay of a vehicle founded upon a guilty plea. The court found that the creation of the Magistrate's Court was constitutional.

Shephard v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


749 S.W.2d 283; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1127



April 27, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT #5 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment by the County Criminal Court #5 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6011-1 (1988). Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in admitting the videotape of appellant immediately following his arrest over objection and in overruling a motion to suppress the videotape.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6011-1 (1988). On appeal, appellant contended that the trial court erroneously admitted the videotape of appellant immediately following his arrest and overruled a motion to suppress the videotape. The court rejected these contentions and affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that the videotape was properly admitted over objection because the erasure of a portion of the videotape was accidental and was sufficiently explained so that its presence did not affect the reliability and trustworthiness of the videotape. The court determined that the motion to suppress the videotape was correct. The court reasoned that the videotape that depicted appellant after he invoked his right to counsel was not testimonial evidence protected by U.S. Const. amend. V.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of driving while intoxicated. The court found that the videotape of appellant taken shortly after his arrest was properly admitted into evidence because an alteration to the videotape was accidental and sufficiently explained. The court further found that the videotape of appellant was not constitutionally protected testimonial evidence just because he invoked his right to counsel.

Rogers v. State

April 26, 1988, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 8TH DISTRICT COURT OF HOPKINS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of Hopkins County (Texas) convicting her of allowing dog fights on her property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with allowing dog fights on her property. The jury convicted her and assessed punishment at four years confinement and a $ 2000 fine. The imposition of sentence was suspended and defendant was placed on probation for four years. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that no search warrant was required by the police because Fourth Amendment protection did not extend to defendant's open field. OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant of allowing dog fights on her property was affirmed because Fourth Amendment protection did not extend to defendant's open field. The dog pit was located on defendant's property in an open section of the woods nearly 400 yards from defendant's mobile home.

Fras v. State


No. 01-87-00520-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 875

NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 462,554.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment at life and a monetary fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and was assessed a fine and life imprisonment. On appeal, the court held that considering the totality of the evidence adduced at both phases of the trial, and because of the egregiousness of defendant's acts and his prior criminal record, the trial court's inclusion of the parole charge was harmless. The court held that defendant's requested charge was adequately covered by the court's charge and affirmed the trial court's ruling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that convicted defendant of aggravated sexual assault and assessed punishment at life and a monetary fine. The court held that considering the totality of the circumstances and defendant's egregious behavior, the inclusion of a parole charge was harmless, that defendant's confession was made voluntary, and the arrest following the confession was legal.

Landrum v. State


Nos. 05-87-00277-CR, 05-87-00278-CR, 05-87-00279-CR, 05-87-00280-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


751 S.W.2d 530; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1553



April 18, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of a district court of Dallas County (Texas), that convicted her of unlawful delivery of amphetamines, possession of amphetamines, and possession of cocaine on the grounds that it was error to deny her motion to suppress evidence and her motion to dismiss the indictments because of violations of the speedy trial act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of her convictions for unlawful delivery of amphetamines, possession of amphetamines, and possession of cocaine alleging that her motion to suppress evidence should have been granted and that her indictment should have been dismissed. The court affirmed the convictions finding that the arresting officers had jurisdiction. The court reasoned that even though the officers were outside of their city limits, Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 341.021(e) gave them jurisdiction throughout the county. The court determined that the speedy trial act (act) had previously been declared unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine of the Texas Constitution by encroaching on a prosecutor's exclusive prosecutorial discretion in preparing for trial. As a result, the court found that appellant had no rights pursuant to that act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions finding that it was proper to deny the motion to suppress evidence because the arresting police officers were operating within their jurisdiction at the time of the arrest and search, and appellant had no rights pursuant to the speedy trial act because it had previously been declared unconstitutional.

Gregor v. State


No. 01-87-00892-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 810



April 14, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court At Law No. 7, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 954,146.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of the misdemeanor offense of unlawfully possessing with intent to promote obscene material which was entered by the County Criminal Court At Law No. 7, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of unlawfully possessing with intent to promote obscene material. Defendant appealed contending that the trial court erred in denying his pre-trial motion to quash because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21, the statute forming the basis of this action, was indefinite, uncertain, and vague. The court held that the statute had been found not to be vague. Defendant further argued that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(1)(A), which defined obscene in terms of the average person applying contemporary community standards, was unconstitutional. The court held that the contemporary community standard was still to be applied when determining whether the work, as a whole, appealed to the prurient interest in sex, and § 43.21(a)(1)(A) remained constitutional. Defendant also argued that his conduct could not be considered criminal because no judicial determination of obscenity was made prior to the transaction forming the basis of this proceeding. The court concluded that defendant failed to raise this issue in his pre-trial motion to quash, therefore, it was not preserved for appeal. Thus, the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because defendant failed to raise the issues he argued on appeal in his pretrial motion to quash which formed the basis of his appeal.

 

916 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rahmani v. State


No. 01-87-00551-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


748 S.W.2d 618; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 819



April 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 05848173.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3 of Harris County (Texas), which affirmed defendant's conviction for operating an adult arcade without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the trial court's affirmation of the municipal court's conviction of defendant for operating an adult arcade without a permit. Defendant contended that the city code violated U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV because the ordinance was overbroad, void for vagueness, and it effected an impermissible prior restraint on free speech. The court noted that the only actual effect of the ordinance was that patrons of adult arcades would be required to peruse openly, under specified minimum lighting, the entertainment provided. The court found that the ordinance left open ample alternative channels of communication. Furthermore, the court determined that any restriction on first amendment freedoms that might have resulted from enforcement of the ordinance was no greater than was essential to the furtherance of the governmental interests involved. The court also determined that the ordinance was not overbroad because it was precise in its language and limited in its reach. The ordinance was found to be clear, not vague. The court determined that the ordinance was not a prior restraint. Accordingly, the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for operating an adult arcade without a permit, because the court determined that the ordinance was not overbroad, vague, or a prior restraint on free speech.

 

917 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Nugent v. State


No. 13-86-490-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


749 S.W.2d 595; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 887



April 14, 1988, Decided  
April 14, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which convicted appellant of involuntary manslaughter and sentenced him to a 10-year probated sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter. Appellant argued that the trial court failed in its charge to apply law to the facts regarding the issue of concurrent cause, that the trial court erred in its instruction as to legal presumption of intoxication, that it was error to sentence appellant to 120 days in jail as a condition of probation, and that a mandatory requirement of confinement as a condition to probation denied appellant of equal protection of the law. The court reversed and held that a charge that did not apply the law to the facts failed to lead the jury to the threshold of its duty which was to decide the fact issues. The court stated that the trial court should have applied the law of concurrent causation to the facts of this case. The court held that the trial court erred in its instruction in that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05 (1988) contained its own definition of intoxication. The court held that it was purely legislative function to establish a range of punishment and that confinement as a condition of probation was rational. The court remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction of involuntary manslaughter and remanded for a new trial because the trial court should have charged the jury on applying the law of concurrent causation to the facts of the case. The court held that the jury instruction as to presumption of intoxication was improper because the statute appellant was charged under contained its own definition of intoxication.

 

918 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gilliam v. State


No. 11-87-011-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


749 S.W.2d 582; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 720



April 7, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Haskell County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury found her guilty of delivery of a controlled substance being less than 28 grams of amphetamine, appellant sought review of her conviction and sentence imposed by a Haskell County trial court (Texas). Appellant challenged the admission of extraneous offenses, the refusal to give a lesser included jury instruction, improper remarks by appellee state to the jury, and the instruction that the jury could consider good time and parole.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of a controlled substance being less than 28 grams of amphetamine and sentenced to confinement for three years. On appeal, the court held that evidence of her extraneous offenses was admissible to refute appellant's defense of entrapment. The court found that the probative value of testimony regarding appellant's other drug transactions with undercover agents outweighed its prejudicial aspects. Because appellant admitted in her testimony that she had delivered amphetamine to an agent, the court concluded that she was not entitled to a lesser included instruction on possession. Although comments by appellee state to the jury on doing something about drugs could have been improper, the court found that the jury was told to disregard the remarks and that the error did not warrant a mistrial. Noting that the sentence imposed was on the low end of the punishment range, the court held that the impermissible instruction on parole and good-conduct time did not contribute to appellant's sentence. Finding no reversible error, the court affirmed the judgment against appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence for delivery of a controlled substance being less than 28 grams of amphetamine. The court found that evidence of extraneous offenses was admissible to refute entrapment defense, that she was not entitled to a lesser included charge, that appellee's remarks to do something about drugs was followed by an instruction to disregard, and that the parole charge did not contribute to her sentence.

Cook v. State


No. 01-87-00435-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 652



March 31, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 464,588.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found appellant guilty of possession of phencyclidine.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of possession of phencyclidine. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellant contended that he was denied effective assistance of counsel and that the trial court's charge on the parole laws was reversible error. The record indicated that appellant was afforded complete discovery, and no harm had been shown. Appellant failed to show any discoverable evidence that was not found or that he had been harmed. The attorney laid the proper predicate for introducing pictures into evidence after the court reminded him of the proper procedure. The attorney did not fail to raise an objection where the objection made after non-responsive testimony could have cause the jury to speculate. The court found that the attorney's trial strategy at voir dire was insufficient to support the claim although another attorney might have used different tactics. The court found that the prosecutor did not discuss the parole charge and there was no egregious harm requiring reversal.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for possession of phencyclidine was affirmed. Appellant did not show that he received ineffective assistance of counsel or that the trial court's charging the jury on the parole law was reversible error.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying habeas corpus relief to release appellant on his own recognizance because he failed to show that bond was excessive.

Huresti v. State


No. 01-87-00526-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 686



March 31, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 466,755.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 232nd District Court Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft and enhanced his sentence because of four prior convictions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft. The court affirmed that conviction as reformed to delete the text and the jury further found that a deadly weapon, to wit, a firearm, was used during the commission of this offense on appeal. The court found that the jury instruction on the parole charge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1988), was unconstitutional, but held that it was not a reversible error. The court concluded that the evidence against appellant was overwhelming, that the state's jury argument did not mention of the possibility of parole, and that appellant reminded the jury that they were not to consider the parole law's application. The court further held that it was improper to convict appellant of using a deadly weapon because neither the indictment nor any special plea informed him that the state would seek a deadly weapon finding. The court also found that evidence of appellant's misdemeanor convictions was admissible because the statutory requirement as to a written jury trial waiver only applied to felonies, and that his guilty plea for his felony to the jury was considered a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft as reformed to delete and the jury further found that a deadly weapon, to wit, a firearm, was used during the commission of this offense. The court held that an unconstitutional instruction was not a reversible error because the issue of parole was properly managed, but that there was inadequate notice of appellant's deadly weapon charge.

Kowey v. State


No. C14-87-00267-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the 337th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(2) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellant grabbed the complainant from behind, pushed her against a wall, blindfolded and bound her, and raped her in a vacant house. Appellant was sentenced to life imprisonment for aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(2) (1987). Appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that appellant had a speedy trial because he was not prejudiced by the one and one-half year delay that resulted from his being tried and incarcerated for other offenses. The court found that the rapes had distinguishing characteristics common to the offense charged, including victims acting as real estate agents, appellant ripping the crotch out of their underwear, and appellant telling them that he wanted their money.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault because appellant was afforded a speedy trial, the conviction was supported by sufficient evidence that appellant committed aggravated sexual assault, and the trial court properly admitted evidence of appellant's similar extraneous offenses to prove his identity.

Cartmill v. State


No. 05-87-00190-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


748 S.W.2d 581; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1004



March 31, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF COLLIN COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of a district court of Collin County (Texas), which found him guilty of aggravated sexual assault of a 12-year-old girl and sentenced him to 15 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a 12-year-old girl and sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment. Appellant sought review, contending that the trial court denied him his right of confrontation under the United States and Texas Constitutions by allowing the state to introduce a videotaped interview of the complainant. The videotape was introduced by the state after the complainant had been cross-examined by appellant's counsel, who attempted to impeach her based on statements she made in the interview. The court overruled appellant's point of error and affirmed the conviction, holding that the videotape was admissible because it was introduced in response to appellant's attempt to impeach the witness with her interview to show that the statements were consistent with the trial testimony. The court held that since the tape was admissible, appellant's constitutional right to confront the witness against him was not violated. The court also held that any error in admitting the videotape would have been harmless because under the totality of the evidence, such error would not have affected the jury's decision to convict or assess punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment convicting appellant of aggravated sexual assault. The court held that a videotaped interview of the complainant was admissible and that appellant's constitutional right to confront the witness was not violated. The court held further that, even if the videotape had not been admissible, any error in admitting it would have been harmless considering the totality of the evidence in the case.

Lapasnick v. State


Appeal No. 04-87-00179-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


751 S.W.2d 880; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 1485



March 31, 1988, Decided  
March 31, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Motion for Rehearing, Filed May 24, 1988, Reported at: 751 S.W.2d 880 at 882.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 383,906, Honorable Timothy Johnson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County, Trial Court (Texas), which denied appellant habeas corpus relief for a charged offense of driving while intoxicated. Appellant alleged that his prosecution was barred since a prior charge for the same offense was dismissed when appellee state failed to comply with the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1988).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with driving while intoxicated. The trial court denied appellant habeas corpus relief. Appellant alleged that his prosecution was barred since a prior complaint and information that charged him with the same offense were dismissed due to appellee state's failure to comply with the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1988). On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of habeas corpus relief. The court found that appellant's argument that his prosecution was barred and that he was entitled to discharge was based on Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 (Supp. 1988), which provided that if an accusation was set aside for failure to provide a speedy trial, appellant would be discharged and such discharge would bar any further prosecution of the offense charged. However, the court determined that both articles were declared unconstitutional. The court ruled, therefore, that appellant was not permitted to rely on those statutes as a bar to his prosecution since an unconstitutional statute is void from its inception and could not provide a basis for any right or relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order which denied appellant habeas corpus relief since the Speedy Trial Act and another statute appellant relied upon were unconstitutional. The court held that appellant could not rely on those statutes as a bar to his prosecution since the statutes were void from their inception and could not provide appellant a basis for any right or relief.

Thomas v. State


No. 01-87-00546-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


748 S.W.2d 539; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 582



March 24, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 17,893, Ogden Bass, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, for robbery and alleged that the trial court committed fundamental error when it submitted the charge to the jury on the parole law pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1988), since the statute was unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred when it refused to allow expert witness testimony in regard to eyewitness testimony.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state introduced evidence of appellant's prior felony and misdemeanor convictions. Appellee also elicited testimony from appellant that he was on parole for an aggravated robbery conviction. Appellant was convicted of robbery. On appeal, the court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1988), was unconstitutional and the jury charge given pursuant to the statute was unconstitutional. However, since there was no objection at trial, the harm to appellant had to be egregious. The court found that the jury instruction was not egregious error and that there was no evidence that the parole charge influenced the jury's assessment of punishment since the sentence appellant received was at the lower end of the punishment spectrum and therefore the court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court also determined that the trial court did not err when it refused to allow appellant's expert witness, a psychologist, to testify about the reliability of eyewitness testimony. The court held that such expert testimony was an inadmissible attack on the credibility of a lay witness, and that cross-examination should be used to attack the lay witness' credibility instead.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction since although the jury charge submitted on the parole law was unconstitutional, the jury charge error was not egregious error. Also, the trial court did not err when it refused to allow expert witness testimony about the reliability of eyewitness testimony since such testimony was an inadmissible attack on the credibility of a lay witness.

Porter v. State


No. C14-87-00486-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 615



March 24, 1988, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 460,028.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas for aggravated sexual assault of a child. Defendant alleged that he was denied his right to a speedy trial and to his right of compulsory process.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pled guilty pursuant to a plea agreement and agreed to a written stipulation of evidence he was convicted of the offense of aggravated sexual assault of a child. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the trial court did not err when it denied defendant's motion to dismiss on statutory speedy trial grounds because defendant did not have a constitutional or statutory right to a speedy trial in Texas. The court also held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977), which forbade a conviction upon a guilty plea unless appellee prosecution produced sufficient evidence to support the judgment, did not deprive defendant of his right to compulsory process or prohibit him from cross-examining appellee's witnesses and calling rebuttal witnesses. The court held that the trial court was not required to get an express waiver of the right to compulsory process from the defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child from the trial court was affirmed because he did not have a right to a speedy trial, and he was not deprived of his right to compulsory process.

Adame v. State


No. 01-87-00122-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 626



March 24, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 453,982.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted felon challenged the order of the 248th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which instructed the jury under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07(4) and found him guilty of delivery of less than 28 grams of heroin after overruling his challenge to the admission of the heroin into evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant convicted felon sold heroin to an undercover officer and was charged with delivery of less than 28 grams of heroin. He was convicted and appealed. On appeal appellant asserted that the trial court erred in admitting the heroin into evidence because the appellee state failed to prove the proper chain of custody. The court affirmed the conviction and held appellee state met its burden of proving care, custody, and control of the heroin from the time it was purchased from appellant to the time of trial. The trial court did not err in admitting the heroin into evidence. The jury was given an unconstitutional jury instruction under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4), but it was harmless error because appellant did not suffer any egregious harm from the instruction. Appellant's assertion that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4) was vague was without merit. The court held the statute was not misleading and appellant suffered no egregious harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant of delivery of less than 28 grams of heroin and held that the heroin was properly admitted into evidence because the chain of custody of the heroin was properly established. The court also held that any error in having given the jury the parol jury instruction was harmless because appellant did not suffer any egregious harm..

Valle v. State


No. 2-87-098-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


747 S.W.2d 541; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 836



March 23, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 1 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 1 of Tarrant County (Texas), which accepted appellant's guilty plea and convicted him of the offense of theft of property valued between $ 750 and $ 20, 000. Appellant asserted that the guilty plea was not voluntary.


OVERVIEW: In July 1986, appellant stole an automobile valued between $ 750.00 and $ 20,000.00. In April 1987, appellant appeared at a hearing to answer charges alleged in the indictment against him. Appellant waived his right to a jury trial and agreed to stipulate to testimony. He signed an agreement in which he stipulated to evidence and knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his rights. Appellant pleaded guilty to the offense alleged, without the benefit of a plea bargain agreement. He was sentenced to thirty-five years confinement in the Texas Department of Corrections because he answered "true" to two enhancement paragraphs alleging prior felony convictions. On appeal, appellant challenged the voluntary nature of his guilty plea. The court affirmed the conviction because the procedure followed by the court on the record substantially followed Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 26.13 (1988), and the fact that appellant hoped to get a more lenient sentence by virtue of his guilty plea was not the type of wrong which art. 26.13 was designed to protect against.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of theft of property valued in excess of $ 750, because his guilty plea made at hearing prior to trial with the assistance of counsel and on the record was voluntary, informed, and knowledgeable. The fact that appellant hoped to get a more lenient sentence from the court than the jury did not impair the fairness of the guilty plea.

 

929 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Duc Vu v. State


No. 6-87-027-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


750 S.W.2d 8; 1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 580



March 22, 1988, Decided  
March 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

Appealed from the 202nd Judicial District Court of Bowie County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for voluntary manslaughter in the 202nd Judicial District Court of Bowie County, Texas. The trial court refused to instruct the jury about the law of parole and good time under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) ( Supp. 1988), and gave an oral Allen charge to the jury during its deliberations without tendering a written charge to defendant for examination prior to its being read to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of voluntary manslaughter and sought further review. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that defendant was not entitled to an instruction about the law of parole and good time as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, §4(a) (Supp. 1988), because the requested instruction was prejudicial to defendant and § 4(a) was unconstitutional. The court held that the trial court's Allen charge was not harmful error because it was phrased in a manner that would not coerce the jurors into reaching a verdict just for the sake of reaching a verdict. Finally, the court found that defendant failed to preserve for review his contention that the Allen instruction should have been tendered to defendant for examination in writing before it was read to the jury under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 36.27 (1981). Defense counsel objected that the charge was not in writing but did not object to the failure to tender at trial. The court held that an objection to a failure to follow statutory procedures was necessary to preserve a claimed error when the trial court gave an Allen charge to a deadlocked jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's voluntary manslaughter convictions. Defendant was not entitled to an instruction on parole and good time because it was prejudicial to defendant. The Allen charge was not harmful because it did not coerce the jurors. Defendant failed to preserve for review his claim that the trial court did not follow statutory procedures because he did not object to the Allen charge on that ground at trial.

Palmire v. State


No. 01-87-00082-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1988 Tex. App. LEXIS 544



March 17, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 438,736.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which found sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction of murder, allowed the state to reopen its case in chief after both sides had rested and allowed a submission to the jury on parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for murdering his stepfather and challenged the conviction claiming that there was insufficient evidence to support the conviction, that it was an abuse of discretion to allow the state to reopen its case in chief after both sides had rested and that allowing the submission of parole to the jury had the effect of enhancing his punishment. The court affirmed the conviction and found that the accomplice's testimony was independently corroborated by the fact that other witness' testified about defendant talking about the murder and by the fact that defendant's signature was on the contract-for-termination. The court found that the decision to allow the state to reopen was soundly within the discretion of the trial court and defendant failed to show how he was harmed by the reopening and therefore the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The court found that defendant was not denied a fair and impartial trial because the jury was told by the state that they were not allowed to discuss the effect of parole and there was no evidence that indicated that the parole instruction influenced the jury to enhance the punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder because there was sufficient incriminating evidence outside the accomplice testimony that tended to corroborate the accomplice's testimony, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the state to reopen its case in chief after both sides had rested and there was no evidence that submitting the issue of parole to the jury enhanced defendant's punishment.
