965 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Richards v. State


No. 01-86-00780-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


743 S.W.2d 747; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9154



December 31, 1987, Decided  
December 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 906,325.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of violating the seat belt law by a municipal court that was affirmed in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11, Harris County (Texas). The primary issue in this case was the constitutionality of the Texas seat belt law. Appellant contended that the law violated the due process and the equal protection clauses of the Texas and United States Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of violating the seat belt law by a municipal court; on appeal the county criminal court at law affirmed. On appeal thereafter, appellant challenged the constitutionality of the seatbelt law, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, sec. 107C (Supp. 1987). Appellant contended that the seatbelt law violated the due process and the equal protection clauses of the Texas and United States Constitutions by taking away his liberty interest found in U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court noted that the liberty interest was guaranteed to be free from arbitrary interferences, but was not immunity from reasonable regulations. The court found that the imposition of a state seatbelt law was a reasonable exercise of state power in that it bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest that was not arbitrary or discriminatory, i.e., keeping public roads safer. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment against appellant, overruling his contentions of error. The court concluded that appellant failed to show how the Texas seatbelt law was unconstitutional as it applied to him. The court also concluded that the Texas seatbelt law was constitutional because it bore a rational relationship to the legitimate legislative purpose of reducing injuries and/or fatalities in traffic accidents.

 

966 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. State


No. A14-86-400-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9162



December 31, 1987, Decided  
December 31, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 16,526.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for aggravated kidnapping from the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County, (Texas). On appeal, appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence in both enhancement paragraphs, the trial court's failure to instruct on a lesser included offense, the admission of a statement by appellant's co-defendant, and the court's instruction to the jury on good conduct time and parole.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping in the trial court. Appellant challenged his convictions pointing out errors with the insufficiency of the evidence in both enhancement paragraphs, the trial court's failure to instruct on a lesser included offense, the admission of a statement by appellant's co-defendant, and the court's instruction to the jury on good conduct time and parole. The court looked at the first two errors asserted by appellant together and agreed that the state had erred in presenting the enhancement paragraphs. The court noted that a conviction that was appealed from was not final until affirmed by the appellate court and the issuance of a mandate. In this case, the state had failed to prove that the conviction alleged in the first paragraph, attempted burglary of a habitation, became final prior to the commission of the offense alleged in the second paragraph, aggravated robbery. The court stated that because the state did not meet its burden of proof as to either enhancement paragraph, it was precluded from use of the enhancement paragraphs on retrial. The trial court judgment was reversed and remanded for a new trial on punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment against the appellant for aggravated kidnapping, and remanded the case back for a new trial on punishment. The court found error with the state's presentation of the enhancement paragraphs that were to be used to enhance the appellant's sentence in that the first conviction had not been properly shown as final, thus the state had not proven this was final prior to commission of the second enhancement.

 

967 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rodriguez v. State


No. 04-86-00069-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


743 S.W.2d 287; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9241



December 31, 1987, Decided  
December 31, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPELLANT'S MOTION FOR REHEARING. Reported at: 743 S.W.2d 287 at 294.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of November 12, 1987, Reported at: 743 S.W.2d 287. Appeal from the 25th District Court of Guadalupe County, Trial Court No. 83-657, Honorable Gus J. Strauss, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a motion for rehearing with the court, after it affirmed his conviction from the 25th District Court, Guadalupe County (Texas), arguing that the jury charge was erroneous, and that he was entitled to a reversal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged and convicted of a criminal offense. Appellant challenged his conviction, arguing that the jury charge given under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) was erroneous because the statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the jury charge was not unconstitutional. Appellant then filed a motion for rehearing, arguing that recent binding court precedent had held that the jury charge was unconstitutional. The court determined that in light of the new authority holding the statute unconstitutional, it was error for the jury to be charged pursuant to art. 37.07, § 4(a). However, the court determined that the error was harmless, because the error occurred at the punishment phase of the trial, and appellant received the exact number of years he asked for, albeit without probation. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, and overruled the motion for rehearing.


OUTCOME: The court overruled appellant's motion and affirmed the conviction, stating that even though it was error for the jury to be charged in accordance with an unconstitutional state statute, the error was harmless because it occurred at the punishment phase of the trial, and appellant received the exact number of years he asked for, albeit without probation.

 

968 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Tarlton v. State


Nos. 05-86-01040-CR, 05-86-01041-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


748 S.W.2d 13; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9287



December 31, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of delivery, and aggravated delivery, of marijuana by a District Court, Dallas County (Texas) pursuant to open pleas of guilty. On appeal, appellant contended error in the refusal of the lower court to permit him to plead anew or to withdraw his prior pleas because they were not intelligently entered into and voluntarily made.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to delivery, and aggravated delivery, of marijuana and was convicted in the trial court; he then appealed. Appellant, although sentenced improperly, had not advised the trial court of the error through any type of motion, and did not attempt to withdraw the guilty plea. The criminal appeals court remanded to the trial court for resentencing. Appellant also had filed a petition for discretionary review in the criminal appeals court, contending that the appeals court erred in holding that he could not enter a not guilty plea upon remand. The court found that the criminal appeals court erred in failing to remand the cause for resentencing. The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed and the case remanded to the trial court for resentencing. At the remand hearing, appellant told the trial court that he had been incorrectly admonished as to the penalty range and sought to plea anew or withdraw his prior pleas. The trial court held that it had no discretion to allow that. On appeal, the court affirmed because the mandate of the criminal appeals court did not allow a lower court to act under its own discretion to consider appellant's request.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, holding that mandates of the criminal appeals court had to be literally read and applied and that only that court was able to interpret or amend its mandates in light of subsequent developments. The trial court was without power to permit withdrawal of the pleas of defendant to delivery, and aggravated delivery, of marijuana.

Severn v. State


No. 6-87-016-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


744 S.W.2d 280; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9123



December 30, 1987, Decided  
December 30, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 188th Judicial District Court of Gregg County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 188th Judicial District Court, Gregg County (Texas), which found him guilty of indecency with a child, arguing that the trial court erred in admitting a videotaped interview with the complainant child as part of the state's case-in-chief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with indecency with a child. As part of the state's case-in-chief, the trial court allowed the prosecutor to introduce into evidence a videotaped interview with the complainant child in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.071 (1986). The complainant child also testified at trial, and was subject to cross-examination. Appellant was found guilty of the charge, and challenged his conviction, arguing that videotape of the interview violated his right to confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Tex. Const. art. I, § 10. Appellant also claimed that the videotape violated his right to due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. The court held that because art. 38.071 had previously been declared unconstitutional, appellant was not required to object to the admission of the videotaped interview. The court determined that, based upon binding court precedent, the trial court erred in admitting the taped interview, because it violated appellant's right to confrontation and due process. The court reversed the conviction, and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, and held that appellant's right to confrontation and due process were violated by the trial court allowing the prosecutor to introduce a taped interview of the complaining witness during appellant's trial for indecency with a child. The court remanded for a new trial.

Rodgers v. State


No. 2-86-280-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


744 S.W.2d 281; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9244



December 30, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) of aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon, and sentenced to fifty years confinement. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of trial court and remanded the cause for a new trial of punishment only. The court held that the trial court committed reversible error in admitting evidence of a previous judgment and sentence of appellant for theft of property in order to enhance or increase appellant's minimum punishment for the committed offense, because appellant was on shock probation for this earlier offense at the time he committed the aggravated robbery, and his probation had not been revoked. Accordingly, there was no "final judgment" of this previous conviction for enhancement purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the cause for a new trial of punishment only. The court ruled that the trial court improperly admitted evidence of a previous judgment and sentence of appellant for a previous crime for enhancement of appellant's sentence, when such prior judgment was not a final judgment.

 

971 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Luken v. State


No. 01-86-00576-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


744 S.W.2d 274; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9107



December 24, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 444,450, C. V. MILBURN, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 232nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, after a jury found him guilty of felony burglary of a habitation with intent to commit sexual assault and found that he used a deadly weapon in the commission of the offense. The jury then found the enhancement paragraph allegation true and assessed punishment of confinement for 75 years.


OVERVIEW: Upon being arrested for an unrelated felony, appellant made a written confession, admitting that he had committed an assault on complainant. The jury found him guilty of felony burglary with intent to commit sexual assault and found that he used a deadly weapon. The jury also found the enhancement paragraph allegation true. Appellant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence. The court withdrew its original opinion in this matter and substituted the present opinion, which reformed the judgment so that the phrase "affirmative finding of a deadly weapon" was deleted. The court stated that the original opinion did not take notice of case law which required the State to "plead" that it would seek an affirmative finding of deadly weapon use in either the indictment or by a special plea as authorized by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 27.01(1966). While the court found no evidence that appellant's attorney was surprised or hampered in his ability to defend appellant, the court stated that notice to appellant personally was required and that any evidence reflecting notice or lack of harm was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court reformed the judgment so that the phrase "affirmative finding of a deadly weapon" was deleted, in light of case law which required the State to plead its intention to seek an affirmative finding of deadly weapon use regardless of evidence of notice or lack of harm. In all other respects, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Tuan Van Truong v. State


No. A14-85-877-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


744 S.W.2d 954; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9092



December 23, 1987, Decided  
December 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 180th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 404,040.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the 180th District Court Harris County, Texas, judgment of conviction for indecency with a child, violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of indecency with a child, violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11. The court affirmed the conviction. The court also held that appellant failed to raise any issues pertaining to the trial court's jury instructions violating the separation of powers at trial, thereby waiving appellate review. The court also held that an instruction on the law of parole contained in the charge of the court did not warrant reversal because appellant failed to object at trial to the instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of indecency with a child because the jury instructions used did not deprive appellant of any substantive vested right and appellant failed to object to the instruction on the law of parole.

Smith v. State


No. 3-85-321-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


742 S.W.2d 847; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9208



December 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMAL COUNTY, 207TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR-85-2B, HONORABLE ROBERT T. PFEUFFER, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the 207th Judicial District Court of Comal County, Texas, on conviction for the offense of aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(5) (1987). The trial court assessed punishment at confinement for 20 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for the offense of aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(5) (1987). The trial court assessed punishment at confinement for 20 years. The judgment was affirmed on count one and vacated on count two of the indictment. The court rejected defendant's contention that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court found that counsel's decision to elect punishment by the court, thereby precluding defendant from consideration for probation, could have been based upon counsel's mistaken belief of the trial court's ability to grant probation or a trial strategy as the case concerned the aggravated sexual assault of a three-year-old, a crime the jury panel expressed its distaste for throughout the trial. Further, defendant failed to establish a reasonable probability the jury would have granted him probation. Based on defendant's unequivocal confession and other evidence, defendant also failed to show that had counsel objected to the introduction of videotape prepared in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2(1987) and had the tape been excluded, the outcome of the trial would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to count one of the indictment holding that defendant failed to established he was denied effective assistance of counsel, that there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction, and that his unequivocal confession was not voluntarily given. The court vacated the judgment as to count two of the indictment as both counts of aggravated assault arose out of the same transaction.

Bells v. Greater Texoma Utility Authority


No. 05-85-00996-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


744 S.W.2d 636; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9256



December 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF GRAYSON COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted appellee Greater Texoma Utility Authority's motion for rehearing, withdrew former opinions and substituted the instant opinion. Appellants, city and mayor, sought review of a judgment from a district court of Grayson County, Texas, that declared appellee was constitutionally created and its actions, particularly the issuance of certain bonds, constitutionally taken. All parties were enjoined from challenging these issues.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Greater Texoma Utility Authority desired to use certain property purportedly voluntarily annexed by appellant city as a landfill site. In an action brought along with the landowner it sought to have annexation of the land declared void. Appellants, city and its mayor, alleged that appellee was an improper party plaintiff as it was unconstitutionally created, did not exist as an entity which could bring suit, and had engaged in various void actions. Appellee then brought a class action suit for a declaratory judgment under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 717m-1(1986) to have appellant city, its actions, and specifically a bond issuance declared constitutional. Appellants sought review of that declaratory judgment. The court vacated the actions of the trial court and dismissed the cause. The court found that appellee undisputedly failed to literally comply with the Open Meetings Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-17(1987), that substantial compliance was not sufficient, and that as a result of a meeting held in violation of the Act, appellants were placed in the position of posting a $ 2,000,000 bond or losing any claim it had against appellee.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the actions of the trial court and dismissed the cause, holding that appellee Greater Texoma Utility Authority's actions which authorized the action for a declaratory judgment were invalid as appellee failed to literally comply with the Open Meetings Act (Act) so that appellants were not properly served with process and a default judgment was rendered against them.

Castillo v. State


No. 01-87-00063-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9034



December 17, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Cause No. 388,021


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the sentence imposed by the 339th District Court Harris County (Texas), after appellant was convicted of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft and punishment was assessed at 45 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft and assessed his punishment at 45 years confinement. The court affirmed the sentence. The court found no error in allowing the prosecution to state that "if you can't do the time, don't do the crime." The court held that the prosecutor did not improperly request that the jury assess a particular punishment by asking them to listen to the demands of the community in his closing arguments, but rather asked the jury to be the voice of the community. The court also held that the prosecutor's reference to parole amounted to harmless error. The court held that the jury was properly instructed not to consider how the parole laws would affect appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence imposed on appellant's conviction for burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft because the prosecutor's argument on not committing crime unless able to do the time was found to be a proper plea for law enforcement, and the jury was properly instructed not to consider how the parole laws would affect appellant.

Omniphone, Inc. v. Southwestern Bell Tel. Co.


No. 3-87-207-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


742 S.W.2d 523; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9193



December 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 414,292, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of judgment in favor of appellee telephone companies in a declaratory judgment suit on a tariff under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 22.221(a), in the 299th District Court of Travis County (Texas). Specifically, appellants challenged the denial of their request for injunctive relief from appellees' disconnection of their "976" service.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought review of denial of injunctive relief in favor of appellee telephone companies in a suit to have a tariff declared invalid under Tex. Gov't Code § 22.221(a), in connection with the disconnection of their "976" number for violations of the applicable tariff. The court affirmed the judgment, explaining that its review was limited to a determination of whether the order denying the application for a temporary injunction was an abuse of discretion. The court concluded that no abuse of discretion was shown when the lower court could have properly concluded that no state action and discriminatory motive existed as to appellees' decision to disconnect. The court rejected the argument that the district attorney's call to appellees was such coercive state action when appellees had already completed an investigation that determined that appellants were in violation of the tariff. The court further determined that there was no abuse of discretion by the lower court in its conclusion that no unlawful discrimination existed in the prohibition of live communication on the "976" service because a reasonable basis for appellees' dissimilar treatment was shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying appellants injunctive relief and declaring appellee telephone companies' tariff valid. The court held that no abuse of discretion in the decision existed because appellants failed to demonstrate a reasonable probability of success on the merits, as unreasonable discrimination did not exist and the decision to disconnect service was not a product of state action.

Martinez v. State


Nos. A14-87-559-CR, A14-87-560-CR, A14-87-561-CR, A14-87-562-CR, A14-87-563-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


744 S.W.2d 224; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8996



December 10, 1987, Decided  
December 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 1279; On Appeal from the County Criminal Court At Law No. 12, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 1223; On Appeal from the County Criminal Court At Law No. 14, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 1225; On Appeal from the County Criminal Court At Law No. 2, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 1227; On Appeal from the County Criminal Court At Law No. 9, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 1220


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the decision of several County Criminal Courts at Law, Harris County (Texas), which affirmed their convictions in municipal court for operating adult arcades without a permit. Defendants alleged that the city ordinance prohibiting their conduct was vague, overbroad, and violated due process of law, and constituted a prior restraint of free speech.


OVERVIEW: The appeals of numerous defendants of their convictions for violation of an ordinance regulating adult arcades were consolidated for appeal. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The ordinance made clear what it prohibited. When the ordinary meanings of the statutory words were applied, the ordinance was clear as to what it provided. The standards given in the ordinance, coupled with the permit application and denial provisions, were sufficient to prevent arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement by the police chief. The police chief was afforded no discretion under the ordinance but was required to grant the permit if the requirements of the ordinance were met. The court held that the ordinance was not directed at any constitutionally protected conduct or material but was clearly a regulation of the business of adult arcades. The ordinance was not a prior restraint on free speech because the ordinance sought to meet important governmental interests which were within the power of a city government and those interests were unrelated to the suppression of free expression.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions for violating a city ordinance regulating the operation of adult arcades were affirmed on the grounds that the ordinance was not impermissibly vague, overbroad, nor a prior restraint of free speech.

Ivan Dement, Inc. v. Stratford Independent School Dist.


No. 07-87-0105-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


742 S.W.2d 820; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9143



December 10, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SHERMAN COUNTY; 69TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. A-511; HONORABLE BILL SHEEHAN, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the 69th District Court, Sherman County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, school, hospital, and county, for ad valorem taxes on his personal property. Appellant claimed there were fact questions which precluded summary judgment, that the administrative remedy was unconstitutional, and that summary judgment was precluded by provisions of Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. §§ 21.02 and 42.09.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner sought review of the lower court's grant of summary judgment to appellees, school, hospital, and county, for ad valorem taxes. Appellant claimed there were fact questions which precluded summary judgment, that the administrative remedy was unconstitutional, and that summary judgment was precluded by Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. §§ 21.01 and 42.09. Appellant claimed he paid taxes in the county of his principal place of business and was not responsible for taxes in a county where he rented property to keep equipment. The court found that the property tax code met due process requirements because it included a right of protest and a right of appeal, but that administrative remedies must be first exhausted before there could be a judicial challenge to a tax assessment. Because appellant did not exhaust administrative remedies, his constitutional argument was overruled. The court held that tax statements and the affidavit of a tax collector that the statements were true and correct was sufficient evidence to support a prima facie showing of appellant's liability for the taxes. The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court that awarded ad valorem taxes to appellees, school, hospital, and county, was affirmed. Appellant property owner failed to exhaust his administrative remedies, the property tax code met due process requirements and was constitutional, and appellees established prima facie evidence that appellant was liable for the taxes.

Milam v. State


No. 05-87-00210-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


742 S.W.2d 810; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9204



December 8, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Dismissed May 9, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 72.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction after a guilty plea in a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), for possession of phenylacetone with intent to manufacture amphetamine, alleging that the statute under which he was convicted was applied retroactively and the scope of the search which led to the seizure of the contraband exceeded the authorization of the search warrant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of phenylacetone with intent to manufacture amphetamine and pleaded guilty. On appeal challenging the application of the statute to his factual situation, the court reversed. The court held that on the date of defendant's arrest, possession of phenylacetone alone was not proscribed by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 2.04(f)(2). The court held that the amended statute, as applied to defendant, constituted an unconstitutional retroactive application of the law. The failure to charge defendant with criminally prohibited conduct prevented the instrument presented by the grand jury from meeting the constitutional requirements of an indictment. Defendant's failure to object to the instrument was not fatal to his appeal. Because the instrument presented to the trial court did not constitute an indictment, the trial court's jurisdiction was not invoked. Such an error constituted a jurisdictional defect which the court had the power to consider pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 40.


OUTCOME: Conviction for possession of phenylacetone with intent to manufacture amphetamine reversed and the purported indictment dismissed on the grounds that the ex post facto application of the law resulted in an instrument which failed to allege a criminal offense and defendant did not waive the right to complain of the lack of an indictment vesting the trial court with jurisdiction.

Industrial Acci. Bd. v. Magana


No. A14-86-898-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


742 S.W.2d 799; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8897



December 3, 1987, Decided  
December 3, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 281st District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-25185.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee insurance company employees filed a motion to dismiss the appeal of appellant industrial accident board, which sought review of a judgment from the 281st District Court, Harris County (Texas), permanently restraining from pursuing an investigation into appellees' allegedly unfair claims handling practices, said appellees contending that the court lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 140.


OVERVIEW: Appellee insurance company employees obtained an order that permanently enjoined appellant industrial accident board from pursuing an investigation of appellees for alleged unfair claims handling practices. Appellant sought review of that order and, in so doing, did not designate an appellate court in its notice of appeal. However, the record indicated that appellant requested a record of the proceedings from the trial court and directed that it be forwarded to the supreme court, where it thereafter actively pursued the appeal. The supreme court dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction. Appellant thereafter sought review in a regular appeal, and appellees filed a motion to dismiss for want of jurisdiction. The court granted appellees' motion, finding that pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 140, appellant had the option of pursuing a regular appeal or a direct appeal to the supreme court. The court concluded that once appellant elected one form of appeal, that decision foreclosed the option of the other form of appeal. The court held that once the direct appeal was dismissed, appellant had no further avenue of review left.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion of appellee insurance company employees to dismiss the action of appellant industrial accident board for want of jurisdiction, finding that appellant had elected to appeal the issuance of a restraining order directly to the supreme court and that upon dismissal of that appeal, there was no further ground to pursue a second appeal.

Bonner v. State


No. 01-86-01007-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8900

NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 428,855


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of murder, alleging that the trial court erred in allowing the prosecutor to use a peremptory challenge to strike black venire members, in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. XI and XIV.


OVERVIEW: The jury found defendant guilty of murder. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in allowing the prosecutor to use a peremptory challenge to strike black venire members, in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. VI and XIV. Defendant proved that the prosecutor struck three Hispanics and three blacks from the venire on peremptory challenges. Defendant then offered the prosecutor's jury list into evidence and rested. The prosecutor testified that he had made no notes of any venire member's race, denied that his motives were racial, and pointed out that he did not strike two other black venire members. The jury consisted of 11 whites and one Hispanic. The court found that defendant failed to establish disparate treatment of different jurors and did not point outs facts suggesting discrimination. Affirming the conviction, the court held that defendant failed to make a prima facie case of purposeful discrimination in the prosecutor's exercise of peremptory challenges.

982 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Garner v. State


No. B14-87-00263-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8902



December 3, 1987, Decided & Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 208th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 455,097.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant sought review of a conviction from the 208th District Court, Harris County (Texas), for two counts of aggravated robbery, each enhanced by one prior felony conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a convenience store and went to the cooler to get a soft drink. Appellant then nodded to a companion who was outside. The companion entered with a gun and robbed the store's clerk. A customer, joined by a police officer, chased the robbers' car. They found the car abandoned, and they found appellant in the vicinity using a public telephone. The customer identified appellant as one of the robbers. Appellant was charged with two counts of aggravated robbery, each enhanced by one prior felony conviction. The jury found appellant guilty, and he was punished accordingly. Appellant challenged the conviction, claiming multiple points of error. The court held that appellant failed to specify which evidence should have been suppressed; thus, the error was not preserved. In addition, the arrest was lawful because there was insufficient time to obtain a warrant before appellant would have escaped. There was sufficient evidence that linked appellant with the commission of the crime. Therefore, the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery was affirmed because appellant failed to preserve his evidence challenge for review, his arrest was lawful because of exigent circumstances, and there was sufficient evidence that linked appellant with the commission of the crime.

Mills v. State


No. 86-00705-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8933



December 3, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 442,353.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him, upon a jury trial, of voluntary manslaughter, contending his due process rights were violated when the state failed to inform him of its intention to submit a deadly weapon finding and error in overruling his objection to the state's closing argument urging improper expectations of the community.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his conviction for voluntary manslaughter, claiming that his due process rights were violated when the state failed to inform him of its intention to seek an affirmative finding of use of a deadly weapon and error in overruling his objection to the state's closing argument improperly urging the expectations of the community. The court sustained defendant's allegation concerning the deadly weapon finding, concluding that the state had to provide notice of its intentions to submit a deadly weapon finding and failure to provide such notice was fundamental error. The court ordered that the trial court's affirmative finding on the deadly weapon issue be deleted, but that defendant's conviction was affirmed in all other respects. The court concluded that the state's argument to the jury did not improperly exert the expectations of the community, but was a plea to the jury to do its duty to assess a proper punishment for the crime committed. The court determined that after viewing the evidence in a light most favorable to the verdict, any rational trier of fact could have found all the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court sustained defendant's allegation that the trial court improperly overruled his objection to the state's failure to inform him of its intention to seek a deadly weapon finding, determining that failure to provide such notice was a fundamental error. The court ordered that the trial court's affirmative finding on that issue be deleted from the judgment but that in all other respects the court affirmed the conviction of defendant.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for discretionary review of the decision of the 357th District Court, Cameron County (Texas), that imposed a sentence of nine years imprisonment and a fine for his conviction of sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault and sentenced to nine years confinement and a fine. Defendant filed for discretionary review in light of an opinion of the court of appeals that held that the parole and good conduct charge authorized by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1987) was unconstitutional. The court found that because the error claimed by defendant concerned a jury instruction, harmless error was the test of review. Ali v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


742 S.W.2d 749; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9201



November 25, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of theft of property for writing a check for commercial food products for which there was insufficient funds in defendant's bank account.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for theft of property and sentenced to 20 years in prison after writing a check with insufficient funds for commercial food products. Defendant asserted several points of error on appeal, but the reviewing court affirmed. OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for theft of property was affirmed. The court held that evidence of prior similar transactions and a surveillance videotape were admissible, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant, the state's peremptory challenge did not violate equal protection, and the trial court's instructions cured any improper jury arguments.

Rankin v. State


No. C14-87-033-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8801



November 19, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 451,359.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the 177th District Court Harris County (Texas), for the offense of forgery. Defendant waived trial by a jury and pled not guilty to the offense. The court found him guilty as charged and assessed his punishment at 60 years confinement in the Texas Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the indictment was fundamentally defective, and that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to dismiss for violation of the Speedy Trial Act. Defendant also argued that there was no evidence that he possessed the forged instrument with an intent to harm or defraud. Finally, defendant asserted that he was induced to sign a written waiver of a jury trial by the false representations of his trial counsel and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel at trial. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's arguments and affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that there was no defect in the indictment, and that defendant did not meet his burden of rebutting the state's prima facie showing of compliance with the Speedy Trial Act with evidence demonstrating that the state was not actually ready for trial during the prescribed time period. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient to show knowledge on the part of defendant that the check was forged and to show he acted with intent to defraud or harm. Finally, the court held that trial counsel was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which found defendant guilty of forgery. The court held that there was no defect in the indictment, that defendant did not rebut the state's prima facie showing of compliance with the Speedy Trial Act, that the evidence was sufficient to show intent to defraud or harm, and that defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective.

 

987 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Weatherly v. State


No. 01-87-00317-CR .


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8827



November 19, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 435,778


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the 337th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which, pursuant to a plea bargain agreement, found defendant guilty of burglary of a building and assessed punishment under the plea bargain at 10 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty, pursuant to a plea bargain agreement, to the charge of burglary of a building and was sentenced to 10 years confinement. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss for denial of a speedy trial and that his conviction was based on a plea that was not made knowingly and voluntarily. The court held that defendant's complaint regarding a speedy trial was moot because the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1987), violated the separation of powers doctrine by unconstitutionally controlling the prosecutor's exclusive discretion in preparing for trial. The court held that a plea of guilty was involuntary where the terms of a plea bargain were impossible to fulfill, and a guilty plea would not support a conviction if that plea was motivated by significant misinformation conveyed by the court or one of its officers. The court held that nothing in the record showed any misinformation was conveyed by the court or its officers and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that, pursuant to a plea bargain agreement, found defendant guilty of burglary of a building, and assessed punishment under the plea bargain at 10 years confinement. The court held because the claim regarding a speedy trial was moot and because the record reflected that no misinformation was conveyed by the court or its officers, defendant's guilty plea was voluntary.

Pryor v. State


No. B14-86-641-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8832



November 19, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 337th District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 437,404.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the 337th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of murder. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in admitting photographs of the victim into evidence, that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction, and that a jury instruction pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed and held that the burden to present a sufficient record under Tex. R. App. P. 50(d) was on defendant. Thus, when defendant did not include the photographs in contention as part of the record, his contention was overruled. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant when the evidence was viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict, even though the facts showed some evidence of self-defense, because the jury was the sole judge of witness credibility. The court found that art. 37.07, § 4 was not vague and had been held constitutionally valid on many occasions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of murder. The court held that defendant failed to include photographs that he contended were inadmissible as part of the record, that there was sufficient evidence to convict him, and that a statute regarding a jury instruction was constitutional.

Vasquez v. State


No. 04-87-00029-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


740 S.W.2d 120; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8966



November 18, 1987, Decided  
November 18, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 341st District Court of Webb County, Trial Court No. 19,857, Honorable Elma T. Salinas Ender, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 341st District Court of Webb County (Texas), that convicted appellant of involuntary manslaughter by reason of intoxication pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §19.05(a)(2)(1974). Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in declaring a mistrial on its own motion due to the absence of a juror and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6b(c) was unconstitutional and not applicable.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with involuntary manslaughter by reason of intoxication pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(2)(1974). A jury was selected but one juror felt she was related to victim and a mistrial was granted. A second jury was selected but one juror was absent and a mistrial was declared. Appellant moved for dismissal. The trial court denied the motion and a third jury was selected that found appellant guilty. The trial court imposed a special condition of probation pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6b(c) (1987) requiring appellant to serve 120 days in confinement after the jury assessed probation. Appellant contended the trial court erred in declaring a mistrial and retrial was barred by double jeopardy. He argued that art. 42.12, § 6b(c) denied him rights and was not applicable when the jury recommended probation. The appellate court affirmed and held the trial court did not abuse its discretion in declaring a mistrial and the subsequent retrial was not barred. The court ruled that there was no infringement of appellant's rights and the trial court had the authority to require appellant to serve 120 days as a condition of probation.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter by reason of intoxication was affirmed. The court ruled that when appellant elected not to proceed with 11 jurors present, the trial court properly declared a mistrial. Additionally, the applicable statute clearly mandated the trial court to require as a condition of probation that appellant serve not less than 120 days in a penal institution.

Lighter v. State


No. 09-86-254 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


741 S.W.2d 568; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9178



November 18, 1987, Decided  
November 18, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 221ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF MONTGOMERY COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 221st Judicial Court of Montgomery County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. The court reversed, holding that admission into evidence of a photo album depicting sexually explicit photographs was error because it had been seized pursuant to a defective search warrant. In so ruling, the court noted that the affidavit for the search warrant contained neither the date the offense occurred, nor the date that the album was seen in appellant's residence. Further, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23(b) (1979), which provided for the admission of evidence obtained in good faith upon a warrant based on probable cause, was not effective on the date the seizure took place. In addition, the admission of a videotape of the complaining witness was not unconstitutional because she appeared in the trial court immediately after the tape was shown, and was cross-examined by appellant. Further, the trial court correctly instructed the jury that the state was not bound by the exact date set forth in the indictment, but could convict if they found that the offense occurred within five years preceding the return of the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault, because the admission, during trial, of a photo album depicting sexually explicit photographs was reversible error because it was seized pursuant to a defective search warrant.

Roberson v. State


No. 6-87-005-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


741 S.W.2d 563; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8807



November 17, 1987, Decided  
November 17, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 71st Judicial District Court of Harrison County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 71st Judicial District Court of Harrison County (Texas), which convicted him of theft. Appellant claimed that the trial court erroneously denied his attorney's motion to withdraw, that he was denied a speedy trial, and that the trial court erred in enhancing his sentence to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for theft as a result of passing a worthless check in exchange for merchandise sold in a store. The charged offense, otherwise a misdemeanor, was upgraded to a third degree felony because of two prior convictions under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(C) (1987), which punished a third theft offense as a felony regardless of the value of the property stolen. Appellant was found guilty and the jury enhanced his punishment to life imprisonment, because of the two prior felony convictions. Appellant contended that the state failed to allege and prove that his second felony conviction for manslaughter used to enhance his punishment was for an offense that occurred after the first felony was final. On appeal, the court held that while the state properly alleged that appellant's second felony conviction was for an offense that occurred after his first felony conviction was final, it failed to prove that allegation. As result, the court reversed and remanded appellant's conviction to the trial court. It further provided that upon retrial, appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter could not be used to enhance his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision to convict appellant of theft. The court held that the trial court erred when it used appellant's prior manslaughter conviction to enhance his sentence because the state failed to prove that appellant's manslaughter conviction, the second felony used to enhance appellant's sentence, was for an offense that occurred after the first felony was final.

Ann. art. 4413 (29bb), § 13. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the indictment was not fundamentally defective. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413 (29bb), § 3.

Bonilla v. State


No. 01-86-00616-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


740 S.W.2d 583; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8770



November 12, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 432,046.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for murder following a jury trial in the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder. He challenged the conviction on several grounds. The court affirmed, first concluding that the district court did not err when it prevented appellant's counsel from questioning prospective jurors about their ability to recommend probation for an illegal alien because the question had no bearing on any issue in the case. Next, the court held that the district court did not err by admitting the written confession appellant gave following his warrantless arrest because the arrest was lawful. The court found that the arrest was lawful because the officers had satisfactory proof that a murder had been committed, that appellant committed it, and that appellant was likely to flee. Based on its finding that the arrest was lawful, the court also determined that counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to the admission of the confession as the fruit of an illegal arrest. Further, the court determined that appellant waived his objection to the jury instruction on the issue of parole and his objection to the authority of the district judge to preside over the trial by failing to raise contemporaneous objections at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's murder conviction because the district court did not err by preventing counsel from asking potential jurors a question about their ability to recommend parole, the warrantless arrest of appellant was lawful, appellant was not denied the effective assistance of counsel, and appellant waived his remaining claims of error by failing to raise contemporaneous trial objections.

OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery. Punishment was assessed at 50 years' confinement. Appellant sought review of his conviction claiming that the parole law instructions contained in the court's charge to the jury were unconstitutional and that a jury argument made by the prosecutor at the punishment phase of the trial constituted reversible error. The judgment of the trial court was reversed based on appellant's point of error regarding the argument made by the prosecutor at the punishment phase of the trial. The court held that telling the jury to disregard the charge of the court on the applicable law and to apply the parole laws was grossly improper and prejudicial.

Watkins v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


741 S.W.2d 546; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9133



November 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(b) (1987) following a jury trial in a district court of Dallas County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(b). He claimed on appeal that art. 67011-(b) was unconstitutionally vague, the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction, the information was defective, the jury instructions were erroneous, and an officer was erroneously allowed to give expert testimony. The court affirmed, holding that art. 67011-(b) defined the crime of driving while intoxicated with sufficient specificity to pass constitutional muster. Further, the court found that the information was legally sufficient because it tracked the language of art. 67011-(b) and charged every element of the crime. The court also found that the jury instructions regarding the elements of the crime were proper as they tracked the language of art. 67011-(b) and the information. Finally, the court found that appellant waived review of his claim regarding the officer's expert testimony, as his trial objection thereto differed from the point raised on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated because the statute criminalizing such conduct was not unconstitutionally vague, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, the information was legally sufficient, the jury instructions regarding the elements of the crime were proper, and appellant waived review of his claim regarding the expert testimony of a police officer.

Kingsley v. State


No. 05-86-01047-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


744 S.W.2d 191; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9247



November 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of a District Court of Dallas County, Texas, that convicted him of the purchase of a child in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.06. Appellant claimed that § 25.06 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, it was error not to quash the indictment and the jury panel, and it was improper to admit evidence of unadjudicated extraneous offenses during the punishment phase of the trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.06 for the purchase of a child, alleging that § 25.06 was unconstitutionally vague, that the indictment and the jury should have been quashed, and that it was error to permit the state to introduce certain evidence. The court reversed the conviction, concluding that it was reversible error to admit the extraneous unadjudicated offense evidence. The court reasoned that appellant, in presenting three witnesses who testified only that he had never been convicted of a felony, did not mislead the jury or give a false impression to give the state a reason to introduce such unadjudicated offenses. The court found that while the statute may have been vague with respect to some conduct, it clearly prohibited appellant's conduct, so he had no standing to argue vagueness. It further found that appellant failed to meet his burden of demonstrating that the comment made by a potential juror who was later excused prejudiced his rights when the comment, while concerning the case, was made to the pool of potential jurors rather than to the jury itself.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for purchase of a child the conviction and remanded the cause for a new trial, finding that it was reversible error to admit evidence of unadjudicated extraneous offenses when appellant did not mislead or give a false impression to the jury. However, the statute was not unconstitutional with respect to appellant's actions, and there was no error in the indictment or the jury deliberations.

Summertree Venture III v. Federal Sav. & Loan Ins. Corp.


No. C14-86-924-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


742 S.W.2d 446; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8768



November 5, 1987, Decided  
November 5, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 125th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-13940.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a corporation and associated individuals, challenged the decision of the 125th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which set aside a default judgment entered against appellee Federal Savings & Loan Insurance Corporation and dismissed appellants' cause for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a corporation and associated individuals, sued a savings association concerning a foreclosure sale and a construction loan. Appellee Federal Savings & Loan Insurance Company declared the savings association insolvent and was appointed receiver. The trial court entered a default judgment against appellee. Appellants sought review of the trial court's decision to set aside the default judgment and dismiss appellants' cause of action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Appellee asserted that under 12 U.S.C.S. § 1464(d)(6)(c), adjudication of appellants' claims would restrain or affect the exercise of appellee's receivership powers. The court determined that it was not bound by the decisions of the Fifth Circuit or by federal district courts; therefore, the court looked independently at the statutes, regulations, and legislative history for its determination. The court determined that appellee did not have the power to adjudicate claims. Therefore, the court held that dismissal of appellants' action was improper and appellants should have been allowed to proceed with their claim. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of an action by appellants, a corporation and associated individuals, concerning a foreclosure sale and a construction loan. The court determined that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over appellants' claims because Congress had not given appellee Federal Savings & Loan Insurance Corporation the exclusive power to adjudicate claims, so appellants' claim should have been allowed.

 

999 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Douglas v. State


Nos. 01-86-00452-CR, 01-86-00453-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


739 S.W.2d 660; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8642



October 29, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 351st District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Nos. 439,373 & 439,374.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After he pleaded guilty to possession of marijuana and delivery of marijuana, appellant sought review of his conviction from the 351st District Court of Harris County, Texas. Appellant contested the denial of his motions to dismiss on statutory speedy trial grounds and to quash the indictment for statutory defects, and claimed he was denied effective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: After his pretrial motions were denied, appellant pleaded guilty to possession of marijuana and delivery of marijuana and was sentenced to 15 years in prison. On appeal, the court rejected as moot appellant's claim that his motion to dismiss should have been granted on statutory speedy trial grounds because the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1987), had been declared unconstitutional under the separation of powers doctrine. Although the grand jury did not prepare a memorandum before the indictment in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 20.19 (1977), the court held that the indictment was properly not quashed because it was neither defective nor irregular in form or substance. On appellant's claim that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, the court found that he did not show that a different presentation by his counsel would have yielded a favorable outcome on his pre-trial motions. Finding no reversible errors, the court affirmed appellant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for possession and delivery of marijuana because his pre-trial motions were properly denied and he failed to show that his assistance of counsel was ineffective. The court found that appellant's claim for dismissal on speedy trial grounds was moot because the statute had been declared unconstitutional and that the grand jury indictment was not rendered invalid for lack of a memorandum.

 

1000 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Teubner v. State


Nos. A14-86-445-CR, A14-86-446-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


742 S.W.2d 57; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8645



October 29, 1987, Decided  
October 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 262nd District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 449,600.

On Appeal from the 262nd District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 449,601.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both appellants, father and stepmother, challenged a decision from the 262nd District Court of Harris Count (Texas), which convicted them of bodily injury to a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, father and stepmother, were indicted and pleaded not guilty to the charge of bodily injury to a child. The evidence showed that appellants subjected an 11 year-old girl to a series of severe beatings. The jury found them guilty, and the trial court sentenced them to 10 years' confinement and a fine. Appellants sought review, contending that the trial court erred in denying appellants the right to have a jury assess punishment and that the statute did not give them reasonable notice of the degree of conduct constituting serious bodily injury. On appeal, the court affirmed because it found that appellants' elections for jury punishment were not timely filed when they were not filed until after the jury was selected and both appellants had pleaded guilty. Also, the court found that the statute gave parents reasonable notice of the conditions that constituted bodily injury and that no reasonable person could believe that savage beatings were necessary for disciplinary purposes.


OUTCOME: The convictions of bodily injury to a child were affirmed on the ground that the election made by appellants, father and stepmother, for jury punishment were untimely as they were filed after the jury was selected and both appellants had pleaded not guilty. Further, appellants could not have reasonably believed that the savage beatings they inflicted on the child were necessary for disciplinary purposes.
